从前，有一个磨坊主。他有一个美丽的女儿。女儿长大后，他希望她能衣食无忧，嫁个好人家。他想：“如果有优秀的人来向她求婚，我就把她嫁给他的。”过了不久，来了一个看起来很富有的求婚者，磨坊主在他身上找不出什么毛病，于是就答应了要把女儿嫁给他。然而，磨坊主的女儿并没有像一个女孩应该爱自己未婚夫那样爱这个男人，而且也不信任他。每次一见到他或是一想到他，她都会感到一种莫名的恐惧。一次，未婚夫对她说：“虽然你是我的未婚妻，但你还从没去过我家呢。”姑娘答道：“我不知道你家在哪里。”未婚夫说：“我家在那边黑暗的森林里。”姑娘试着推脱，说自己找不到去那儿的路。未婚夫说：“下个星期天你一定得到我家来；我已经邀请了很多客人，到时我会在森林里的路上撒上灰，这样你就能在森林里找到路了。”星期天到了，少女不得不动身了，可她感觉很不安，连她自己也不知道到底是为什么。她在口袋里装满了豌豆和兵豆，好给走过的路做标记。从森林入口处开始，地上就撒了灰迹，她沿着灰迹往里走，但每走一步她都要在路上扔几颗豌豆。走了差不多一整天，她才走到森林的中央，也是森林中最黑暗的地方，那儿坐落着一座孤零零的房子。她不喜欢那座房子，因为它看起来是那么阴暗、凄凉。她走了进去，但屋里鸦雀无声，一个人也没有。突然，一个声音叫道： There was once on a time a miller, who had a beautiful daughter, and as she was grown up, he wished that she was provided for, and well married.He thought, “If any good suitor comes and asks for her, I will give her to him.”Not long afterwards, a suitor came, who appeared to be very rich, and as the miller had no fault to find with him, he promised his daughter to him.The maiden, however, did not like him quite so much as a girl should like the man to whom she is engaged, and had no confidence in him.Whenever she saw, or thought of him, she felt a secret horror.Once he said to her, “Thou art my betrothed, and yet thou hast never once paid me a visit.”The maiden replied, “I know not where thy house is.”Then said the bridegroom, “My house is out there in the dark forest.”She tried to excuse herself and said she could not find the way there.The bridegroom said, “Next Sunday thou must come out there to me; I have already invited the guests, and I will strew ashes in order that thou mayst find thy way through the forest.”When Sunday came, and the maiden had to set out on her way, she became very uneasy, she herself knew not exactly why, and to mark her way she filled both her pockets full of peas and lentils.Ashes were strewn at the entrance of the forest, and these she followed, but at every step she threw a couple of peas on the ground.She walked almost the whole day until she reached the middle of the forest, where it was the darkest, and there stood a solitary house, which she did not like, for it looked so dark and dismal.She went inside it, but no one was within, and the most absolute stillness reigned.Suddenly a voice cried,
“回去吧，回去吧，年轻的姑娘，亲爱的，你进了杀人犯的房子了。” “Turn back, turn back, young maiden dear, ’Tis a murderer’s house you enter here.”
少女抬头一看，发现那声音是墙上挂着的一个笼子里的鸟发出的。它又叫道： The maiden looked up, and saw that the voice came from a bird, which was hanging in a cage on the wall.Again it cried,
“回去吧，回去吧，年轻的姑娘，亲爱的，你进了杀人犯的房子了。” “Turn back, turn back, young maiden dear, ‘Tis a murderer’s house you enter here.”
可年轻的姑娘还是把所有的房间挨个看了一遍。她走遍了所有的房间，却发现房子是空的，里面一个人也没找到。最后，她走到了地窖，一个老态龙钟的老太婆坐在里面，不停地摇着头。“您能不能告诉我，”少女问老太太道，“我的未婚夫是不是住在这里？” Then the young maiden went on farther from one room to another, and walked through the whole house, but it was entirely empty and not one human being was to be found.At last she came to the cellar, and there sat an extremely aged woman, whose head shook constantly.“Can you not tell me,” said the maiden, “if my betrothed lives here?”
“唉，可怜的孩子，”老妇人答道，“你是从哪儿来的？你现在是在一个杀人犯的房子里。你觉得自己是一个待嫁的新娘，但你的婚礼将与死亡相伴。瞧，他们逼我在那儿放一个大锅，里面盛满水。他们要是抓住你，就会残忍地把你剁成碎片放在锅里煮，把你吃掉。他们都是吃人肉的家伙。如果我不可怜你，救你一命的话，你就死了。” “Alas, poor child,” replied the old woman, “whither hast thou come?Thou art in a murderer’s den.Thou thinkest thou art a bride soon to be married, but thou wilt keep thy wedding with death.Look, I have been forced to put a great kettle on there, with water in it, and when they have thee in their power, they will cut thee to pieces without mercy, will cook thee, and eat thee, for they are eaters of human flesh.If I do not have compassion on thee, and save thee, thou art lost.”
随即，老妇人把她藏到了一个大酒桶后面，以免她被强盗们发现。“你要像老鼠一样安静，”她说，“不要弄出什么声音来，也不要乱动，要是被他们发现的话，你就必死无疑了。等晚上这些强盗们都睡了，我们就逃出去；我等这个机会已经等了很久了。”少女刚藏好，那群邪恶的杀人犯们就回来了。他们又拖回了另一个年轻的女孩。他们都醉醺醺的，没人理睬女孩的尖叫和哀号。他们灌了女孩满满的三杯酒：一杯白色的，一杯红色的，还有一杯黄色的。喝完这些，女孩的心就碎成了两半。接着，他们扯掉了女孩漂亮的衣服，把她放在桌上，将她美丽的身体切成一块一块的，又撒上了些盐。可怜的新娘躲在木桶后面吓得浑身发抖，因为她清楚地看到这些强盗给她安排的结局。有一个强盗注意到死去的女孩小指上有一枚金戒指，但他怎么取也取不下来。情急之下，他拿起斧子把那个小指砍了下来。手指飞了出去，飞过木桶，恰巧落到了新娘的怀里。那个强盗点了一支蜡烛四处寻找戒指，却怎么也找不到。另一个强盗说：“你到那个大桶后面找找？”但那老妇人连忙叫道：“过来吃点儿东西吧，明天早上再找也不迟，反正那个手指自己又不会跑掉。” Thereupon the old woman led her behind a great hogshead where she could not be seen.“Be as still as a mouse,” said she, “do not make a sound, or move, or all will be over with thee.At night, when the robbers are asleep, we will escape; I have long waited for an opportunity.”Hardly was this done, than the godless crew came home.They dragged with them another young girl.They were drunk, and paid no heed to her screams and lamentations.They gave her wine to drink, three glasses full, one glass of white wine, one glass of red, and a glass of yellow, and with this her heart burst in twain.Thereupon they tore off her delicate raiment, laid her on a table, cut her beautiful body in pieces and strewed salt thereon.The poor bride behind the cask trembled and shook, for she saw right well what fate the robbers had destined for her.One of them noticed a gold ring on the little finger of the murdered girl, and as it would not come off at once, he took an axe and cut the finger off, but it sprang up in the air, away over the cask and fell straight into the bride’s bosom.The robber took a candle and wanted to look for it, but could not find it.Then another of them said, “Hast thou looked behind the great hogshead?”But the old woman cried, “Come and get something to eat, and leave off looking till the morning, the finger won’t run away from you.”
强盗们说：“老太太说的也对。”于是，他们就不再找戒指了，坐下来开始吃饭。老妇人在他们的酒里放了安眠药，所以他们很快就躺在地窖里打着呼噜睡着了。听到鼾声后，新娘便从木桶后走了出来。她必须得跨过那些成排地躺在地上沉睡着的强盗们，生怕一不小心再吵醒了他们中的哪一个。但上帝保佑，她安全地跨了过去。老妇人跟上她，打开了门，然后她们倾尽全力，以最快的速度匆忙地离开了杀人犯的房子。风已经把先前洒在地上的灰吹走了，但豌豆和兵豆却已经发芽长大，在月光下给她们指明了回去的路。她们走了一整夜，终于在清晨回到了磨坊里。少女把发生的一切都如实告诉了她的父亲。 Then the robbers said, “The old woman is right,” and gave up their search, and sat down to eat, and the old woman poured a sleeping-draught in their wine, so that they soon lay down in the cellar, and slept and snored.When the bride heard that, she came out from behind the hogshead, and had to step over the sleepers, for they lay in rows on the ground, and great was her terror lest she should waken one of them.But God helped her, and she got safely over.The old woman went up with her, opened the doors, and they hurried out of the murderers’ den with all the speed in their power.The wind had blown away the strewn ashes, but the peas and lentils had sprouted and grown up, and showed them the way in the moonlight.They walked the whole night, until in the morning they arrived at the mill, and then the maiden told her father everything exactly as it had happened.
到了举行婚礼的那一天，新郎到了磨坊主那里。磨坊主邀请了所有的亲戚朋友到场。大家都坐在桌边，磨坊主让每人都讲一段故事。而新娘则静静地坐在那儿，什么也不说。于是，新郎对新娘说：“喂，亲爱的，你什么都不知道吗？像其他人一样给我们说个故事吧。”新娘答道：“那我就讲一个梦吧。有一次，我梦到我独自一人穿过一片森林，最后来到一所空无一人的房子里，但墙上挂着一个笼子，里面有一只鸟叫着： When the day came when the wedding was to be celebrated, the bridegroom appeared, and the Miller had invited all his relations and friends.As they sat at table, each was bidden to relate something.The bride sat still, and said nothing.Then said the bridegroom to the bride, “Come, my darling, dost thou know nothing?Relate something to us like the rest.”She replied, “Then I will relate a dream.I was walking alone through a wood, and at last I came to a house, in which no living soul was, but on the wall there was a bird in a cage which cried,
‘回去吧，回去吧，亲爱的姑娘，你进的是一个杀人犯的房子。’然后它又叫了一遍。 ‘Turn back, turn back, young maiden dear, Tis a murderer’s house you enter here.’And this it cried once more.
“亲爱的，我只梦到了这个。随后，我看遍了所有的房间，都是空的，但却让人觉得那么可怕！最后，我走到了地窖，一个一直摇头的很老很老的老太太坐在那儿；我问她：‘我的新郎是不是住在这所房子里？’她答道：‘啊，可怜的孩子，你走进了一个杀人犯的贼窝。你的新郎是住在这里，但他会把你剁成碎片，杀了你，再把你煮了吃掉。’亲爱的，我只是梦到了这些。但那个老太太把我藏在了一个大桶后面。我刚藏好，那些强盗们就拖着一个少女回来了。他们让她喝了白、红、黄三种颜色的酒。随后，她的心就碎成了两半。亲爱的，我只梦到了这些。随后，他们扯掉了她漂亮的衣服，把她美丽的身体放在桌子上剁碎，又撒上盐。亲爱的，我只梦到了这些。其中一个强盗看到那个少女小指上还有一枚戒指，但戒指取不下来，他就拿来一把斧子把那手指砍了下来，但手指飞了出去，越过木桶飞到了我的怀里。这就是那个戴着戒指的手指！”说完这些话后，她把那戴着戒指的手指拿出来给在座的人看。 “My darling, I only dreamt this.Then I went through all the rooms, and they were all empty, and there was something so horrible about them!At last I went down into the cellar, and there sat a very very old woman, whose head shook; I asked her, ‘Does my bridegroom live in this house?She answered, ‘Alas poor child, thou hast got into a murderer’s den, thy bridegroom does live here, but he will hew thee in pieces, and kill thee, and then he will cook thee, and eat thee.’My darling, I only dreamt this.But the old woman hid me behind a great hogshead, and, scarcely was I hidden, when the robbers came home, dragging a maiden with them, to whom they gave three kinds of wine to drink, white, red, and yellow, with which her heart broke in twain.My darling, I only dreamt this.Thereupon they pulled off her pretty clothes, and hewed her fair body in pieces on a table, and sprinkled them with salt.My darling, I only dreamt this.And one of the robbers saw that there was still a ring on her little finger, and as it was hard to draw off, he took an axe and cut it off, but the finger sprang up in the air, and sprang behind the great hogshead, and fell in my bosom.And there is the finger with the ring!”And with these words she drew it forth, and showed it to those present.
那个强盗在少女讲故事时就已经面如土色了。他跳起来想要逃跑，但在座的宾客牢牢地把他抓住了，并将他扭送到了法官那里。后来，他和他的整个团伙因其罪大恶极的行径而被判处了死刑。 The robber, who had during this story become as pale as ashes, leapt up and wanted to escape, but the guests held him fast, and delivered him over to justice.Then he and his whole troop were executed for their infamous deeds.
磨破的舞鞋 The Shoes That Were Danced to Pieces
从前有一个国王，他养育了十二个女儿，一个比一个生得漂亮。她们同住在一个大房间里，床铺紧挨着。每一天晚上国王都会把门锁上，并且还会栓上门栓。但是，每天早上国王开门时总会发现她们的鞋子因为跳舞而磨出了洞。没人知道其中的缘由。于是，国王只好发布告示：如果有谁能发现她们晚上跳舞的地点，便可娶其中一个为妻，并在国王去世后继承王位。但是，若此人在三天三夜之内没有搞清楚，那就要把他处死。很快，有一位王子前来报名，愿意接受这个任务。王子受到了热情的欢迎，晚上被安排住在公主们隔壁的房间。他的床就放在那里。王子要密切观察公主们的动向。为了防止公主们偷偷溜走，去其他地方，她们的房门敞开着。 THERE was once upon a time a King who had twelve daughters, each one more beautiful than the other.They all slept together in one chamber, in which their beds stood side by side, and every night when they were in them the King locked the door, and bolted it.But in the morning when he unlocked the door, he saw that their shoes were worn out with dancing, and no one could find out how that had come to pass.Then the King caused it to be proclaimed that whosoever could discover where they danced at night, should choose one of them for his wife and be King after his death, but that whosoever came forward and had not discovered it within three days and nights, should have forfeited his life.It was not long before a King’s son presented himself, and offered to undertake the enterprise.He was well received, and in the evening was led into a room adjoining the princesses’ sleeping-chamber.His bed was placed there, and he was to observe where they went and danced, and in order that they might do nothing secretly or go away to some other place, the door of their room was left open.
但是，王子的眼皮越来越沉，一会儿便睡着了。他第二天醒来后发现，十二个公主都去跳过舞了，因为她们的鞋子都磨出了洞。第二天和第三天晚上的情形都和第一天一样，结果，王子就被国王毫不留情地处死了。后来又来了应征者自告奋勇，可最后统统被杀了。这时，来了一个受伤的士兵，他不能再参加战斗了，向着国王居住的城镇走去。途中他遇到了一个老妇人，问他要去哪儿。“我自己也不知道。”士兵回答说，又开玩笑地说，“不过我倒是想弄清楚公主们是在什么地方跳舞把鞋子磨出了洞，然后还可以成为国王呢。”“这并不很难。”老妇人说，“你千万不能喝她们晚上给你的酒，而且必须假装睡得很熟的样子。”然后，老妇人给了他一个小斗篷，说道：“你穿上它便会隐身，然后便能偷偷跟在十二个公主后面。”士兵接受了这个好建议，于是壮起胆子到国王那里去报名，并声称自己是合适人选。他同样受到了很好的款待，并穿上了王室的衣服。到了晚上，士兵被带到了公主们前面的房间休息。正当他想上床睡觉时，大公主端着一杯酒过来了。不过他在下巴下方藏了一块海绵，酒全部被海绵吸收，而他自己一滴也没有喝。然后他就躺下了，没过多久便开始打呼噜，就像已经睡熟了一样。十二个公主听到了打鼾声，全都笑了。大公主说：“他同样也会丢掉性命的。”然后，公主们下了床，打开了衣柜、箱子、柜橱，拿出漂亮的衣服，在镜子前梳妆打扮，翩翩起舞，沉醉在要去跳舞的快乐中。只有最小的公主说：“我不知道是怎么回事，你们那么开心，我却感觉不太对劲，不幸就要降临在我们头上了。”“你这个笨蛋，总是怕这怕那的。”大公主说，“难道你忘记了有多少的王子都是徒劳无功吗？就算我不给他吃安眠药，这个小丑也能睡得像死猪一样。”公主们准备就绪后，仔细瞅了瞅士兵。他仍然闭着眼睛，纹丝不动，于是她们相信自己非常安全了。大公主来到了她的床边，轻拍床沿，床随即沉了下去，公主们挨个下去，大公主走在最前面。那个士兵目睹了一切，便毫不犹豫地披上斗篷，跟在了小公主的后面。正下楼时，他不小心踩到了小公主的裙摆。小公主害怕地惊叫起来：“是什么东西？谁拉住了我的裙子？”“别大惊小怪的！”大公主说，“你可能碰到钉子了。”然后，公主们继续向下走。当到达底部时，她们站在了美丽的林荫大道上，叶子都是银色的，亮晶晶的，闪闪发光。士兵想：“我必须收集点证据才行。”于是他折断了一根树枝，发出了咔嚓一声。小公主再次大喊了起来。“一定有什么问题，你们听到咔嚓一声吗？”大公主说：“那是在鸣枪庆祝，庆祝我们这么快就甩掉了那个士兵。”说完，公主们就来到了另一条林荫大道，那里树上都长着金色叶子。最后公主们到了第三条长满钻石叶子的林荫大道。士兵又各折断两根树枝，每一次都发出咔嚓声，小公主吓得直哆嗦。但是，大公主坚持认为那是鸣枪欢迎的声音。公主们继续走，来到了一个大湖边。岸边泊着十二条小船，每一条船上都坐着一个英俊的王子。他们正等待公主们的到来，每个王子都领一个公主上船。士兵坐在了小公主旁边。她的王子说：“今天的船怎么这么重啊，我得用上全身的劲儿才划得动。”“这是怎么回事啊？”小公主说，“天气真热，我快要出汗了。” But the eyelids of the prince grew heavy as lead, and he fell asleep, and when he awoke in the morning, all twelve had been to the dance, for their shoes were standing there with holes in the soles.On the second and third nights it fell out just the same, and then his head was struck off without mercy.Many others came after this and undertook the enterprise, but all forfeited their lives.Now it came to pass that a poor soldier, who had a wound, and could serve no longer, found himself on the road to the town where the King lived.There he met an old woman, who asked him where he was going.“I hardly know myself,” answered he, and added in jest, “I had half a mind to discover where the princesses danced their shoes into holes, and thus become King.”“That is not so difficult,” said the old woman, “you must not drink the wine which will be brought to you at night, and must pretend to be sound asleep.”With that she gave him a little cloak, and said, “If you put on that, you will be invisible, and then you can steal after the twelve.”When the soldier had received this good advice, he went into the thing in earnest, took heart, went to the King, and announced himself as a suitor.He was as well received as the others, and royal garments were put upon him.He was conducted that evening at bed-time into the ante-chamber, and as he was about to go to bed, the eldest came and brought him a cup of wine, but he had tied a sponge under his chin, and let the wine run down into it, without drinking a drop.Then he lay down and when he had lain a while, he began to snore, as if in the deepest sleep.The twelve princesses heard that, and laughed, and the eldest said, “He, too, might as well have saved his life.”With that they got up, opened wardrobes, presses, cupboards, and brought out pretty dresses; dressed themselves before the mirrors, sprang about, and rejoiced at the prospect of the dance.Only the youngest said, “I know not how it is; you are very happy, but I feel very strange; some misfortune is certainly about to befall us.”“Thou art a goose, who art always frightened,” said the eldest.“Hast thou forgotten how many Kings’ sons have already come here in vain?I had hardly any need to give the soldier a sleeping-draught, in any case the clown would not have awakened.”When they were all ready they looked carefully at the soldier, but he had closed his eyes and did not move or stir, so they felt themselves quite secure.The eldest then went to her bed and tapped it; it immediately sank into the earth, and one after the other they descended through the opening, the eldest going first.The soldier, who had watched everything, tarried no longer, put on his little cloak, and went down last with the youngest.Half-way down the steps, he just trod a little on her dress; she was terrified at that, and cried out, “What is that?who is pulling my dress?”“Don’t be so silly!” said the eldest, “you have caught it on a nail.”Then they went all the way down, and when they were at the bottom, they were standing in a wonderfully pretty avenue of trees, all the leaves of which were of silver, and shone and glistened.The soldier thought, “I must carry a token away with me,” and broke off a twig from one of them, on which the tree cracked with a loud report.The youngest cried out again.“Something is wrong, did you hear the crack?”But the eldest said, “It is a gun fired for joy, because we have got rid of our prince so quickly.”After that they came into an avenue where all the leaves were of gold, and lastly into a third where they were of bright diamonds; he broke off a twig from each, which made such a crack each time that the youngest started back in terror, but the eldest still maintained that they were salutes.They went on and came to a great lake whereon stood twelve little boats, and in every boat sat a handsome prince, all of whom were waiting for the twelve, and each took one of them with him, but the soldier seated himself by the youngest.Then her prince said, “I can’t tell why the boat is so much heavier today; I shall have to row with all my strength, if I am to get it across.”“What should cause that,” said the youngest, “but the warm weather? I feel very warm too.”
在湖的另一边，有一座壮观的宫殿，里面传出了美妙的乐曲声、锣鼓声。他们上岸后走进宫殿。每个王子都带着自己心爱的公主翩翩起舞。士兵也在跳，但是没有人看见他。只要有哪位公主想要举起酒杯喝酒时，士兵都会跑过去把酒喝完。于是酒杯每到嘴边却总是空的。小公主非常害怕，但是大公主每次都让她不要声张。公主们一直跳到鞋子磨出了洞，这时已经是凌晨三点了，她们不得不离开。王子们再划船把公主们送回湖边。士兵这次跟大公主坐在了一起。到了对岸，公主同王子告别，并约定今天晚上再见。公主们走到楼梯处，士兵抢先一步跑了上去，又躺在了床上。十二位公主拖着疲惫的身子慢慢走上来时，士兵已经鼾声如雷，好让公主们听得到。她们说道：“看他的情形，我们是安全的。”公主们把她们漂亮的裙子脱下来放在一边，把跳舞磨破的鞋子放在床下，然后睡觉了。第二天早上，士兵决定先不说，继续观察那美妙的场景。接下来的两天夜里士兵都跟着去了。每次都同第一次一样，公主们把鞋子磨出洞后才回来。但是第三天晚上，士兵带回了酒杯作为证据。国王问讯的时候到了，士兵带上三根树枝和酒杯前去拜见国王。公主们都站在了门后，听着他要说些什么。国王问他：“我的十二个女儿晚上在什么地方跳舞把鞋子磨破了？”士兵回答说：“是在地下的一座宫殿里和十二位王子一起跳舞。”然后叙述了整个过程，同时拿出了证据。于是，国王就把公主们召来，问她们士兵说的是不是事实。公主们知道秘密泄露了，没有办法再隐瞒，就全部招了。然后，国王就问士兵愿娶哪个公主作为妻子。士兵说：“我也不年轻了，就娶大公主吧。”婚礼就在当天举行，国王承诺在死后由他继承王位。但是，地下的王子们被施了很多天的魔法，天数刚好是他们与公主们跳舞的天数。 On the opposite side of the lake stood a splendid, brightly-lit castle, from whence resounded the joyous music of trumpets and kettle-drums.They rowed over there, entered, and each prince danced with the girl he loved, but the soldier danced with them unseen, and when one of them had a cup of wine in her hand he drank it up, so that the cup was empty when she carried it to her mouth; the youngest was alarmed at this, but the eldest always made her be silent.They danced there till three o’clock in the morning when all the shoes were danced into holes, and they were forced to leave off; the princes rowed them back again over the lake, and this time the soldier seated himself by the eldest.On the shore they took leave of their princes, and promised to return the following night.When they reached the stairs the soldier ran on in front and lay down in his bed, and when the twelve had come up slowly and wearily, he was already snoring so loudly that they could all hear him, and they said, “So far as he is concerned, we are safe.”They took off their beautiful dresses, laid them away, put the worn-out shoes under the bed, and lay down.Next morning the soldier was resolved not to speak, but to watch the wonderful goings on, and again went with them.Then everything was done just as it had been done the first time, and each time they danced until their shoes were worn to pieces.But the third time he took a cup away with him as a token.When the hour had arrived for him to give his answer, he took the three twigs and the cup, and went to the King, but the twelve stood behind the door, and listened for what he was going to say.When the King put the question, “Where have my twelve daughters danced their shoes to pieces in the night?” he answered, “In an underground castle with twelve princes,” and related how it had come to pass, and brought out the tokens.The King then summoned his daughters, and asked them if the soldier had told the truth, and when they saw that they were betrayed, and that falsehood would be of no avail, they were obliged to confess all.Thereupon the King asked which of them he would have to wife?He answered, “I am no longer young, so give me the eldest.”Then the wedding was celebrated on the self-same day, and the kingdom was promised him after the King’s death.But the princes were bewitched for as many days as they had danced nights with the twelve.
平鱼 The Sole
鱼王国里不施行规章秩序，长期以来鱼儿们为此心存不满。没有一条鱼会为其他鱼转身让道，而是全都左来右去游得随心所欲，它们要么突然扎进结队游泳的鱼群，要么挡了它们的道；大鱼用鱼尾一扫，小鱼就被驱赶到一边，有时大鱼干脆二话不说直接把小鱼吞入腹中。“要是有个国王在我们之中施法度明正义，”鱼儿说，“那该多好！”于是众鱼集会为它们自己选一名君主，此君是要能乘风破浪的击水好手，还要能仗义扶弱。 The fishes had for a long time been discontented because no order prevailed in their kingdom.None of them turned aside for the others, but all swam to the right or the left as they fancied, or darted between those who wanted to stay together, or got into their way; and a strong one gave a weak one a blow with its tail, which drove it away, or else swallowed it up without more ado.“How delightful it would be,” said they, “if we had a king who enforced law and justice among us!” and they met together to choose for their ruler, the one who could cleave through the water most quickly, and give help to the weak ones.
鱼儿们在岸边排成队，梭子鱼尾巴一拍，群鱼纷纷听随号令向前冲去。梭子鱼箭一般飞了出去，鲱鱼、鮈鱼、鲈鱼、鲤鱼，以及其他各类的鱼都跟在它后面。平鱼也在队伍之中，它也想游到目的地夺冠。霎时，欢呼声传来了：“鲱鱼第一名！”“谁第一？”扁平而善妒的平鱼生气地尖叫道，它已经被远远地甩在后面了，“谁第一？”“鲱鱼！鲱鱼得了第一。”别的鱼回答道。“光着身子的鲱鱼？”那充满嫉妒的东西嚷道，“就是那光身子的鲱鱼第一？”从那时起，平鱼的嘴巴就歪向一边，以此作为它善妒的惩罚。 They placed themselves in rank and file by the shore, and the pike gave the signal with his tail, on which they all started.Like an arrow, the pike darted away, and with him the herring, the gudgeon, the perch, the carp, and all the rest of them.Even the sole swam with them, and hoped to reach the winning-place.All at once, the cry was heard, “The herring is first!”“Who is first?” screamed angrily the flat envious sole, who had been left far behind, “who is first?”“The herring!The herring,” was the answer.“The naked herring?” cried the jealous creature, “the naked herring?”Since that time the sole’s mouth has been at one side for a punishment.
玻璃瓶中的精灵 The Spirit in the Bottle
从前有一个贫穷的伐木工人，他起早贪黑辛苦劳作。终于，他有了一些积蓄，便对他的儿子说：“你是我唯一的孩子，我要用我辛苦赚来的血汗钱供你读书；若你能学些实在的手艺，等我老了，腿脚不灵便，只能呆在家里的时候，就靠你来养啦。”年轻人便去了一所高等学校进学，读书勤奋刻苦，他的老师们对他赞赏有加，他也在那里呆了好一段日子。等到他念完两班，但还有其他课程没学的时候，他父亲挣来的微薄积蓄已经全部用完，年轻人不得不回家到父亲身边去。“唉，”父亲伤心地说，“我不能给你更多的钱了，这年头生活艰难，我挣的钱只够我们爷儿俩平日吃饭，一分余钱都没有。”“亲爱的爸爸，”儿子回答说，“别为这事情费心了，如果这是上帝的意愿，那么逆境就会转化成我的优势，我很快就能习惯的。”当父亲想进入森林，靠帮忙垒齐和砍木材来挣钱时，儿子说：“我要和您一起去，帮您干活。”“不，我的儿子，”父亲说，“那对你来说可不容易；你不习惯做重活儿，是不可能受得了的，何况我只有一把斧头，又没有余钱另买一把。”“就去邻居家，”儿子答道，“他会把他的斧头借给你，等我赚到钱再给自己买一把。”父亲便向邻居借了把斧头，第二天一早，天刚蒙蒙亮时，他们俩就出门，一起进了森林。儿子帮父亲干活儿，心里好不愉悦快活。但是到了正午时分，父亲说：“我们要休息一下，吃个午饭，然后再开工。”儿子手中拿着面包说：“你自己休息吧，父亲，我不累；我在森林里四下走走，找几个鸟窝。”“啊，你这个傻孩子，”父亲说，“你为什么要到处乱跑呢？之后你会很累的，连胳膊也抬不起来啦；呆在这儿，坐到我旁边来。”可是，儿子还是进了森林，吃着面包，兴冲冲地注视着绿荫繁茂的树枝之间，看能不能在什么地方发现鸟窝。他为了找鸟窝四处乱逛，最后来到一棵巨大的、看起来很危险的橡树前，这棵橡树少说也有好几百年的历史了，五个人合抱都围不住它。他站定下来，看着老树想：“肯定有许多鸟儿在这里筑巢。”突然，他觉得好像听到一个声音。仔细一听，他发现一个被闷住的声音喊道：“让我出去，让我出去！”他到处看看，可是什么也没有发现；不过，他想这声音可能是从地底下发出来。他叫道：“你在哪儿啊？”那声音回答：“我在下面，在橡树根中间。让我出去！让我出去！”读书人开始松树底下的土，一番刨根究底，终于在一个小小的空隙处找到一个玻璃瓶子。他拿起瓶子，把它对着阳光，然后便看见有个状如青蛙的东西在瓶子里上蹿下跳。“放我出去！放我出去！”它又叫了，读书人觉得不会出什么事，就拔去了瓶塞。倏然间一个精灵从瓶中升起，逐渐长大，而且速度极快，不一会儿功夫便在读书人跟前站定，面目狰狞，个头足抵得上他面前这棵树的一半。“你可知道，”他用可怕的声音喊道，“放我出来你的回报是什么吗？”“不知道，”读书人毫无畏惧地回答，“这我怎么会知道呢？”“那我就告诉你，”精灵喊道，“我必须为此勒死你。”“你应该早点儿告诉我。”读书人说，“因为那样的话，我就该让你一直关着，至于我的头要不要由你处置，你还得问其他许多人。”“管你这儿、那儿有多少人。”精灵说，“你一定会得到你的回报。你以为我在那儿关了这么久是恩赐么。不，那是给我的惩罚。我就是强大的墨丘利乌斯。谁将我放出来，我就勒死谁。”“且慢，”读书人回答道，“别这么急呀。我得先确定你真的被关在这个小瓶子里过，而且那被关的精灵正是你。倘若这事不假，你要能再进去一次，我便相信，然后我就听凭你的处置。”那精灵傲慢地说：“那简直是小菜一碟。”他蜷起身子，把自己变得和刚开始时一般又小又瘦，这样子钻进原来的瓶口，正好通过瓶颈，重新回到瓶子里。他刚一进去，读书人就把拔去的瓶塞重新塞回去，将瓶子丢回橡树根之间的老地方，就这样把精灵骗过去了。 There was once a poor woodcutter who toiled from early morning till late night.When at last he had laid by some money he said to his boy, “You are my only child, I will spend the money which I have earned with the sweat of my brow on your education; if you learn some honest trade you can support me in my old age, when my limbs have grown stiff and I am obliged to stay at home.”Then the boy went to a High School and learned diligently so that his masters praised him, and he remained there a long time.When he had worked through two classes, but was still not yet perfect in everything, the little pittance which the father had earned was all spent, and the boy was obliged to return home to him.“Ah,” said the father, sorrowfully, “I can give you no more, and in these hard times I cannot earn a farthing more than will suffice for our daily bread.”“Dear father,” answered the son, “don’t trouble yourself about it, if it is God’s will, it will turn to my advantage I shall soon accustom myself to it.”When the father wanted to go into the forest to earn money by helping to pile and stack wood and also chop it, the son said, “I will go with you and help you.”“Nay, my son,” said the father, “that would be hard for you; you are not accustomed to rough work, and will not be able to bear it, besides I have only one axe and no money left wherewith to buy another.”“Just go to the neighbour,” answered the son, “he will lend you his axe until I have earned one for myself.”The father then borrowed an axe of the neighbour, and next morning at break of day they went out into the forest together.The son helped his father and was quite merry and brisk about it.But when the sun was right over their heads, the father said, “We will rest, and have our dinner, and then we shall work as well again.”The son took his bread in his hands, and said, “Just you rest, father, I am not tired; I will walk up and down a little in the forest, and look for birds’ nests.”“Oh, you fool,” said the father, “why should you want to run about there?Afterwards you will be tired, and no longer able to raise your arm; stay here, and sit down beside me.”The son, however, went into the forest, ate his bread, was very merry and peered in among the green branches to see if he could discover a bird’s nest anywhere.So he went up and down to see if he could find a bird’s nest until at last he came to a great dangerous-looking oak, which certainly was already many hundred years old, and which five men could not have spanned.He stood still and looked at it, and thought, “Many a bird must have built its nest in that.”Then all at once it seemed to him that he heard a voice.He listened and became aware that someone was crying in a very smothered voice, “Let me out, let me out!”He looked around, but could discover nothing; nevertheless, he fancied that the voice came out of the ground.Then he cried, “Where art thou?”The voice answered, “I am down here amongst the roots of the oak-tree.Let me out!Let me out!”The scholar began to loosen the earth under the tree, and search among the roots, until at last he found a glass bottle in a little hollow.He lifted it up and held it against the light, and then saw a creature shaped like a frog, springing up and down in it.“Let me out!Let me out!” it cried anew, and the scholar thinking no evil, drew the cork out of the bottle.Immediately a spirit ascended from it, and began to grow, and grew so fast that in a very few moments he stood before the scholar, a terrible fellow as big as half the tree by which he was standing.“Knowest thou,” he cried in an awful voice, “what thy wages are for having let me out?”“No,” replied the scholar fearlessly, “how should I know that?”“Then I will tell thee,” cried the spirit; “I must strangle thee for it.”“Thou shouldst have told me that sooner,” said the scholar, “for I should then have left thee shut up, but my head shall stand fast for all thou canst do; more persons than one must be consulted about that.”“More persons here, more persons there,” said the spirit.“Thou shalt have the wages thou hast earned.Dost thou think that I was shut up there for such a long time as a favour.No, it was a punishment for me.I am the mighty Mercurius.Whoso releases me, him must I strangle.”“Softly,” answered the scholar, “not so fast.I must first know that thou really were shut up in that little bottle, and that thou art the right spirit.If, indeed, thou canst get in again, I will believe and then thou mayst do as thou wilt with me.”The spirit said haughtily, “that is a very trifling feat,” drew himself together, and made himself as small and slender as he had been at first, so that he crept through the same opening, and right through the neck of the bottle in again.Scarcely was he within than the scholar thrust the cork he had drawn back into the bottle, and threw it among the roots of the oak into its old place, and the spirit was betrayed.
现在，读书人要回他父亲那儿了，可是精灵却可怜巴巴地哭喊起来：“啊，请放我出去吧！啊，请放我出去吧！”“不行，”读书人回答，“没有第二次了！曾想取我性命的人，我重新把他抓住，就不会放掉。”“如果你放了我，”精灵说，“我就会给你很多很多，你这一辈子都能衣食无忧。”“不行，”年轻人回答说，“你会像第一次那样骗我的。”“你这可是在拿你的好运气开玩笑啊。”精灵说，“我丝毫不会伤害你，只会慷慨地报答你。”读书人心里思忖道：“我就冒一次险，兴许他会遵守诺言，反正他占不了我的上风。”于是他便拿掉瓶塞，精灵同先前一样从瓶里升起，伸展开来，变得同巨人一样高大了。“现在你将得到你的回报。”他说着，交给读书人一个像一贴膏药一样的小袋子，道：“若将一头施于伤口之上，则伤口立即愈合，若将另一头与钢或铁摩擦，它便能易铁成银。”“我来试试。”读书人说罢，走到一棵树前，用他的斧头砍下树皮，用膏药的一头摩擦树。没有树皮的地方马上便合起来长好了。“啊，它是挺管用，”他对妖怪说，“我们这就各走各的吧。”精灵为年轻人放了他而道谢，年轻人也为精灵的礼物道谢，然后回到他父亲那里。 And now the scolar was about to return to his father, but the spirit cried very piteously, “Ah, do let me out!ah, do let me out!”“No,” answered the scholar, “not a second time!He who has once tried to take my life shall not be set free by me, now that I have caught him again.”“If thou wilt set me free,” said the spirit, “I will give thee so much that thou wilt have plenty all the days of thy life.”“No,” answered the boy, “thou wouldst cheat me as thou didst the first time.”“Thou art playing away with thy own good luck,” said the spirit; “I will do thee no harm but will reward thee richly.”The scholar thought, “I will venture it, perhaps he will keep his word, and anyhow he shall not get the better of me.”Then he took out the cork, and the spirit rose up from the bottle as he had done before, stretched himself out and became as big as a giant.“Now thou shalt have thy reward,” said he, and handed the scholar a little bag just like a plaster, and said, “If thou spreadest one end of this over a wound it will heal, and if thou rubbest steel or iron with the other end it will be changed into silver.”“I must just try that,” said the scholar, and went to a tree, tore off the bark with his axe, and rubbed it with one end of the plaster.It immediately closed together and was healed.“Now, it is all right,” he said to the spirit, “and we can part.”The spirit thanked him for his release, and the boy thanked the spirit for his present, and went back to his father.
“你跑到哪儿去啦？”父亲说，“你为什么忘记你的活儿了？我早就说过你做事不会长久的。”“别动气，父亲，我会补救的。”“是要补救啊，”父亲生气地说，“这里面可是实打实的活儿。”“安心啦，父亲，我很快就会把那边那棵树砍下来，让它一折两段。”他便拿起他的膏药，用它摩擦斧头，接着全力向树一砍，可是因为铁已经变成了银，斧头的刃卷了起来。“哎呀，父亲，看你给了我一把多不好用的斧头呀，它都已经弯啦。”父亲惊愕万分，说道：“啊，看看你都做了些什么？现在我要赔人家斧头了，又没有钱财，这就是我从你干的活里得到的回报。”“别生气，”儿子说，“我很快就赔斧头。”“啊，你这个傻瓜，”父亲叫道，“你哪来的钱赔啊？你的所有东西都是我给你的。你脑子里尽是些读书人的小伎俩，对伐木却是一窍不通。”过了一会儿读书人说：“父亲，我真的干不下去了，我们最好放个假吧。”“啊，什么！”他答道，“你以为我会像你一样两手搭在膝上坐着吗？我必须继续工作，但你可以自己回家了。”“父亲，我这是第一次来这个森林啊，我一个人不知道回家的路。就和我一起回去吧。”眼下父亲的气已经消了点儿，最终他口风松了下来，同儿子一起回去了。然后，他对儿子说，“去把你弄坏的斧子卖了吧，看能得几个钱，我再挣回差价，好陪给邻居。”儿子拿了斧子，带去镇上一个金匠那里，金匠测试了一番，又放到天平上称了称，说：“它能值四百泰勒，我这里还没这么多钱呢。”儿子说：“你有多少就给我多少，剩下的我借你。”金匠给了他三百泰勒，剩下的一百记在帐上。儿子这便回到家里说：“父亲，我拿到钱啦，去问问邻居他的斧子要多少？”“我已经问过了，”老人答道，“要一泰勒六格罗申。”“那就给他两泰勒十二格罗申，两倍的价钱足够了；您看呐，我有好多好多钱呢，”说着便给了父亲一百泰勒，又道，“您下半辈子就能不愁吃、不愁穿，过舒心惬意的日子啦。”“我的老天爷啊！”父亲说，“你怎么变得这么有钱啦？”读书人这才把先前所发生的事，他怎样坚信自己的好运，怎样得到这么一大笔财富全部告诉了父亲。不过，拿着剩下的钱，年轻人回到高校继续读书，而且因为他能用他的膏药治愈一切外伤，他便成为了全世界最有名的医生。 “Where hast thou been racing about?” said the father; “why hast thou forgotten thy work?I said at once that thou wouldst never get on with anything.”“Be easy, father, I will make it up.”“Make it up indeed,” said the father angrily, “there’s no art in that.”“Take care, father, I will soon hew that tree there, so that it will split.”Then he took his plaster, rubbed the axe with it, and dealt a mighty blow, but as the iron had changed into silver, the edge turned; “Hollo, father, just look what a bad axe you’ve given me, it has become quite crooked.”The father was shocked and said, “Ah, what hast thou done?now I shall have to pay for that, and have not the wherewithal, and that is all the good I have got by thy work.”“Don’t get angry,” said the son, “I will soon pay for the axe.”“Oh, thou blockhead,” cried the father, “wherewith wilt thou pay for it?Thou hast nothing but what I give thee.These are students’ tricks that are sticking in thy head, but thou hast no idea of wood-cutting.”After a while the scholar said, “Father, I can really work no more, we had better take a holiday.”“Eh, what!” answered he, “Dost thou think I will sit with my hands lying in my lap like thee?I must go on working, but thou mayst take thyself off home.”“Father, I am here in this wood for the first time, I don’t know my way alone.Do go with me.”As his anger had now abated, the father at last let himself be persuaded and went home with him.Then he said to the son, “Go and sell thy damaged axe, and see what thou canst get for it, and I must earn the difference, in order to pay the neighbour.”The son took the axe, and carried it into town to a goldsmith, who tested it, laid it in the scales, and said, “It is worth four hundred thalers, I have not so much as that by me.”The son said, “Give me what thou hast, I will lend you the rest.”The goldsmith gave him three hundred thalers, and remained a hundred in his debt.The son thereupon went home and said, “Father, I have got the money, go and ask the neighbour what he wants for the axe.”“I know that already,” answered the old man, “one thaler, six groschen.”“Then give him him two thalers, twelve groschen, that is double and enough; see, I have money in plenty,” and he gave the father a hundred thalers, and said, “You shall never know want, live as comfortably as you like.”“Good heavens!” said the father, “how hast thou come by these riches?”The scholar then told how all had come to pass, and how he, trusting in his luck, had made such a good hit.But with the money that was left, he went back to the High School and went on learning more, and as he could heal all wounds with his plaster, he became the most famous doctor in the whole world.
真正的新娘 The True Sweethearts
从前有一个年轻漂亮的女孩，但很小就失去了妈妈，继母用尽各种手段折磨她，女孩的生活痛苦不堪。每当继母让她做事，她都不辞辛苦，尽力完成。坏心肠的继母一点也不为之感动，女孩怎么做她都不满意，都感到不够。女孩越是努力，继母越要变本加厉，那个女人想的是如何用更重的担子把她压垮，如何让她的生活更加悲惨。一天继母对她说：“这里有十二磅羽毛，你天黑之前必须撕完，否则就等着挨揍吧。你还想整天游手好闲吗？”可怜的女孩坐下来开始干活儿，泪水从脸颊滚落下来，因为她清楚地知道，这些活儿是不可能在一天内干完的。每当她把撕好的一小堆羽毛放在面前，悲痛地叹气或是合上双手时，羽毛便飞走了，她不得不把它们捡回来，再重新干。她把胳膊肘放在桌子上，双手托着脸，呜咽着：“难道在这个世界上就没有一个人同情我吗？”这时她听到了一个低沉的声音：“孩子，放心吧，我来帮你。”女孩抬起头，看到一个老妇人站在她旁边。她慈祥地拉起女孩的手，说道：“把你的委屈告诉我吧。”老妇人说话温和亲切，女孩便向她诉说了自己悲惨的生活：重担一个接一个，而那些活儿多得做也做不完。“如果天黑之前撕不完这些羽毛，继母就会打我。她威胁我说她一定会的，我知道她说到做到。”她的眼泪又开始往下流，但是慈祥的老妇人说：“孩子，不要怕，休息一会儿，我帮你做。”女孩躺在床上，很快就睡着了。老妇人在堆满羽毛的桌旁坐了下来，她满是皱纹的手甚至连碰都没碰一下，羽绒忽地就飞离了羽茎。十二磅羽毛很快就撕完了，女孩醒来时，地上是一堆堆雪白的羽毛，房子里打扫得干干净净，但老妇人却消失了。女孩感谢上帝，她一直安静地坐到晚上。继母进来看到活儿已干完，不禁大吃一惊。“看吧，你这个笨手笨脚的家伙，”她说，“只要勤勤恳恳，就没有做不到的事。你为什么不再做点别的呢？就知道俩手叉着坐在那儿。”她出去后嘟哝道：“这孩子还能多干些。我一定要让她干更难的活儿。”第二天早上，她对女孩说：“这有个汤匙，你必须用它舀干花园旁边大池塘里的水，如果晚上之前做不完，你知道会有什么后果。”女孩接过汤匙，发现上面全是洞。即使没有洞，用汤匙舀干一池子水也是不可能的。女孩马上去干活儿，她跪在水边，开始往外舀水，泪水不停地掉进水里。但是慈祥的老妇人再次出现了，她得知女孩伤心的原因之后，说道：“孩子，别难过了。去树林里睡会儿吧，我这就帮你做。”女孩刚走，老妇人只是稍稍碰了下池塘，一片水汽就从水面升起，与云彩混为了一体。池塘渐渐空了，太阳下山之前女孩醒了，她走到池塘边，只看到一些鱼儿在淤泥里挣扎。她走到继母那里，告诉她活儿已经干完了。“应该更早一点干完的！”继母说。她气得脸色煞白，可是很快又想出了新招。第三天早上她对女孩说：“你必须在那片平地上给我盖一座城堡，晚上之前必须盖完。”女孩很惊愕，说：“这样大的工程，我怎么可能干的完啊！”“你给我闭嘴。”继母高声叫喊着，“你能用满是洞的汤匙舀干池塘，那你也能盖完一座城堡。今天我就要住进去，如果缺了什么东西，哪怕是厨房或地下室的小杂碎，你就等着我收拾你吧！”她把女孩赶了出去，女孩走进山谷，里面堆满了石块。她即便用上浑身力气，也搬不动最小的一块。她哭着坐下来，她多么希望老妇人能来帮助她。老妇人很快就来了，她安慰女孩说：“去阴凉处躺下睡会儿吧，我很快就能帮你盖完。如果你喜欢的话，你可以住在里面。”女孩离开后，老妇人轻轻碰了下那些灰色的石块。石块开始上升，很快聚集到一起，就像有巨人在建造墙壁一般。城堡拔地而起，好像有无数双隐形的手在不停地垒着石块。随着地上一声混沌的声响，擎天巨柱高高耸起，自行排列得整整齐齐。屋顶上瓦片排列得错落有致，中午时分，城堡顶部竖起了风标，宛如长衣飘飘的美丽姑娘。夜晚临近时，城堡内部也修饰完了。老妇人是怎样做到的，我无从知晓。房间的墙壁上挂着绸缎丝绒，屋里放着绣着花的椅子，装饰精美的扶手椅配着大理石桌，从天花板垂下的水晶枝形吊灯，映射在光滑的地面上。金笼子里有绿色的鹦鹉，还以很多珍稀的小鸟，唱着最优美的曲调。整个城堡恢宏壮丽，就像给国王准备的一样。太阳快要下山时，女孩醒了，城堡里成千盏明灯映射着她的脸庞。她急冲冲地跑向城堡，穿过敞开的门来到了城堡。台阶上都铺着红布，金色的扶手四周环绕着鲜花盛开的树木。看到富丽的殿堂，女孩站在那儿一动不动，仿佛变成了一块石头。要不是想起了继母，谁知道女孩会在这里伫立多久呢？“啊！”她自言自语道，“希望她能因此而满足，不再折磨我了。”女孩走到继母那，告诉她城堡已经盖好了。“我要马上住进去。”继母说着，从座位上站起来。她们一进城堡，继母不得不用双手挡住眼睛，这里的东西太耀眼了。“你瞧，”她对女孩说，“这对你来说易如反掌，应该让你做些更困难的活儿。”她走遍了所有的房间，仔细检查每个角落，看看是不是有什么缺点或不足，可她却发现不了有什么问题。 There was once on a time a girl who was young and beautiful, but she had lost her mother when she was quite a child, and her step-mother did all she could to make the girl’s life wretched.Whenever this woman gave her anything to do, she worked at it indefatigably, and did everything that lay in her power.Still she could not touch the heart of the wicked woman by that; she was never satisfied; it was never enough.The harder the girl worked, the more work was put upon her, and all that the woman thought of was how to weigh her down with still heavier burdens, and make her life still more miserable.One day she said to her, “Here are twelve pounds of feathers which thou must pick, and if they are not done this evening, thou mayst expect a good beating.Dost thou imagine thou art to idle away the whole day?”The poor girl sat down to the work, but tears ran down her cheeks as she did so, for she saw plainly enough that it was quite impossible to finish the work in one day.Whenever she had a little heap of feathers lying before her, and she sighed or smote her hands together in her anguish, they flew away, and she had to pick them out again, and begin her work anew.Then she put her elbows on the table, laid her face in her two hands, and cried, “Is there no one, then, on God’s earth to have pity on me?”Then she heard a low voice which said, “Be comforted, my child, I have come to help thee.”The maiden looked up, and an old woman was by her side.She took the girl kindly by the hand, and said, “Only tell me what is troubling thee.”As she spoke so kindly, the girl told her of her miserable life, and how one burden after another was laid upon her, and she never could get to the end of the work which was given to her.“If I have not done these feathers by this evening, my step-mother will beat me; she has threatened she will, and I know she keeps her word.”Her tears began to flow again, but the good old woman said, “Do not be afraid, my child; rest a while, and in the meantime I will look to thy work.”The girl lay down on her bed, and soon fell asleep.The old woman seated herself at the table with the feathers, and how they did fly off the quills, which she scarcely touched with her withered hands!The twelve pounds were soon finished, and when the girl awoke, great snow-white heaps were lying, piled up, and everything in the room was neatly cleared away, but the old woman had vanished.The maiden thanked God, and sat still till evening came, when the step-mother came in and marvelled to see the work completed.“Just look, you awkward creature,” said she, “what can be done when people are industrious; and why couldst thou not set about something else?There thou sittest with thy hands crossed.”When she went out she said, “The creature is worth more than her salt.I must give her some work that is still harder.”Next morning she called the girl, and said, “There is a spoon for thee; with that thou must empty out for me the great pond which is beside the garden, and if it is not done by night, thou knowest what will happen.”The girl took the spoon, and saw that it was full of holes; but even if it had not been, she never could have emptied the pond with it.She set to work at once, knelt down by the water, into which her tears were falling, and began to empty it.But the good old woman appeared again, and when she learnt the cause of her grief, she said, “Be of good cheer, my child.Go into the thicket and lie down and sleep; I will soon do thy work.”As soon as the old woman was alone, she barely touched the pond, and a vapour rose up on high from the water, and mingled itself with the clouds.Gradually the pond was emptied, and when the maiden awoke before sunset and came thither, she saw nothing but the fishes which were struggling in the mud.She went to her step-mother, and showed her that the work was done.“It ought to have been done long before this,” said she, and grew white with anger, but she meditated something new.On the third morning she said to the girl, “Thou must build me a castle on the plain there, and it must be ready by the evening.”The maiden was dismayed, and said, “How can I complete such a great work?”“I will endure no opposition,” screamed the step-mother.“If thou canst empty a pond with a spoon that is full of holes, thou canst build a castle too.I will take possession of it this very day, and if anything is wanting, even if it be the most trifling thing in the kitchen or cellar, thou knowest what lies before thee!”She drove the girl out, and when she entered the valley, the rocks were there, piled up one above the other, and all her strength would not have enabled her even to move the very smallest of them.She sat down and wept, and still she hoped the old woman would help her.The old woman was not long in coming; she comforted her and said, “Lie down there in the shade and sleep, and I will soon build the castle for thee.If it would be a pleasure to thee, thou canst live in it thyself.”When the maiden had gone away, the old woman touched the gray rocks.They began to rise, and immediately moved together as if giants had built the walls; and on these the building arose, and it seemed as if countless hands were working invisibly, and placing one stone upon another.There was a dull heavy noise from the ground; pillars arose of their own accord on high, and placed themselves in order near each other.The tiles laid themselves in order on the roof, and when noon-day came, the great weather-cock was already turning itself on the summit of the tower, like a golden figure of the Virgin with fluttering garments.The inside of the castle was being finished while evening was drawing near.How the old woman managed it, I know not; but the walls of the rooms were hung with silk and velvet, embroidered chairs were there, and richly ornamented arm-chairs by marble tables; crystal chandeliers hung down from the ceilings, and mirrored themselves in the smooth pavement; green parrots were there in gilt cages, and so were strange birds which sang most beautifully, and there was on all sides as much magnificence as if a king were going to live there.The sun was just setting when the girl awoke, and the brightness of a thousand lights flashed in her face.She hurried to the castle, and entered by the open door.The steps were spread with red cloth, and the golden balustrade beset with flowering trees.When she saw the splendour of the apartment, she stood as if turned to stone.Who knows how long she might have stood there if she had not remembered the step-mother?“Alas!” she said to herself, “if she could but be satisfied at last, and would give up making my life a misery to me.”The girl went and told her that the castle was ready.“I will move into it at once,” said she, and rose from her seat.When they entered the castle, she was forced to hold her hand before her eyes, the brilliancy of everything was so dazzling.“Thou seest,” said she to the girl, “how easy it has been for thee to do this; I ought to have given thee something harder.”She went through all the rooms, and examined every corner to see if anything was wanting or defective; but she could discover nothing.
“现在我们下楼去，”她恶狠狠地瞪着女孩说，“我还要检查厨房和地下室，要是你落下了什么，休想逃过我的惩罚。”但是壁炉里炉火旺盛，锅里也烧着肉，钳子和铲子斜靠在墙上，亮闪闪的铜器也排列得有条不紊、一目了然。什么都不缺，哪怕是煤箱或是水桶。 “Now we will go down below,” said she, looking at the girl with malicious eyes. “The kitchen and the cellar still have to be examined, and if thou hast forgotten anything thou shalt not escape thy punishment.”But the fire was burning on the hearth, and the meat was cooking in the pans, the tongs and shovel were leaning against the wall, and the shining brazen utensils all arranged in sight.Nothing was wanting, not even a coal-box and water-pail.
“怎么去地下室？”继母喊道，“如果里面没有放满东西，我也不会放过你。”女孩自己一个人打开地板门下去了，但是还没走两步，刚刚放在后面重重的地板门便掉下来了。女孩听到一声尖叫，赶紧抬起门去救继母，可她已经摔了下去，女孩看到她直挺挺地躺在下面，死了。现在恢宏壮丽的城堡属于女孩一个人了。起初，她不知道该如何面对这突然的好运。衣橱里挂着漂亮的裙子，箱子里装满了金银珠宝，女孩要什么有什么。很快女孩的美貌和富有就传遍了整个世界。每天都有追求者上门拜访，但没有一个她喜欢的。终于国王的儿子来了，他搏得了她的芳心，女孩跟他订婚了。城堡的花园里有一棵酸橙树，有一天他们在树下坐着，国王的儿子对女孩说：“我要回家，让父亲同意我们的婚事。我恳求你能在这棵树下等我，不用几个小时我就回来了。”女孩亲了一下他的左脸颊，说：“不要背叛我，也不要让任何人吻你的左脸。我会在这棵酸橙树下等你回来。”女孩一直在酸橙树下等，太阳落山了，他还没有回来。之后的三天，女孩从早等到晚，但仍是徒劳。第四天他仍然没有出现，女孩说：“他一定发生了什么意外。我要出去找他，找不到，我就不回来。”她收拾好三条最漂亮的裙子，第一条镶有闪烁的星星，第二条镶有银色的月亮，第三条镶有金色的太阳，又在手绢里放了一把珠宝，然后出发了。她为找到未婚夫问遍了所有的人，但是没有人见过他，没有人认识他。她游荡到了很远的地方，还是没有找到他。最后，她在一个农夫家里作了放牧女，把裙子和珠宝都埋在了一块石头下面。 “Which is the way to the cellar?” she cried. “If that is not abundantly filled, it shall go ill with thee.”She herself raised up the trap-door and descended; but she had hardly made two steps before the heavy trap-door which was only laid back, fell down.The girl heard a scream, lifted up the door very quickly to go to her aid, but she had fallen down, and the girl found her lying lifeless at the bottom.And now the magnificent castle belonged to the girl alone.She at first did not know how to reconcile herself to her good fortune.Beautiful dresses were hanging in the wardrobes, the chests were filled with gold or silver, or with pearls and jewels, and she never felt a desire that she was not able to gratify.And soon the fame of the beauty and riches of the maiden went over all the world.Wooers presented themselves daily, but none pleased her.At length the son of the King came and he knew how to touch her heart, and she betrothed herself to him.In the garden of the castle was a lime-tree, under which they were one day sitting together, when he said to her, “I will go home and obtain my father’s consent to our marriage.I entreat thee to wait for me here under this lime-tree, I shall be back with thee in a few hours.”The maiden kissed him on his left cheek, and said, “Keep true to me, and never let any one else kiss thee on this cheek.I will wait here under the lime-tree until thou returnest.”The maid stayed beneath the lime-tree until sunset, but he did not return.She sat three days from morning till evening, waiting for him, but in vain.As he still was not there by the fourth day, she said, “Some accident has assuredly befallen him.I will go out and seek him, and will not come back until I have found him.”She packed up three of her most beautiful dresses, one embroidered with bright stars, the second with silver moons, the third with golden suns, tied up a handful of jewels in her handkerchief, and set out.She inquired everywhere for her betrothed, but no one had seen him; no one knew anything about him.Far and wide did she wander through the world, but she found him not.At last she hired herself to a farmer as a cow-herd, and buried her dresses and jewels beneath a stone.
当了放牧女的女孩，每天照看牛群，心情惆怅，满是对爱人的思念。有一只小牛跟女孩关系很好，她每天亲自给它喂草。女孩说： And now she lived as a herdswoman, guarded her herd, and was very sad and full of longing for her beloved one; she had a little calf which she taught to know her, and fed it out of her own hand, and when she said,
“小牛，小牛，跪到我的旁边来，不要像王子忘记在酸橙树下等他的未婚妻一样，忘记我这个牧女。” “Little calf, little calf, kneel by my side, And do not forget thy shepherd-maid, As the prince forgot his betrothed bride, Who waited for him ‘neath the lime-tree’s shade.”
小牛跪在旁边，女孩轻轻地抚摸着它。 the little calf knelt down, and she stroked it.
女孩形单影只，忧心忡忡，一过就是好几年，这时有个消息传遍了全国：国王的女儿将要举行婚礼了。去城里的路经过女孩居住的村庄，有一次，正当女孩放牛时，她的新郎从旁边经过。他得意地骑着马，看都不看周围一眼，女孩一眼就认出了心上人，心里像刺进了一把尖刀。“啊！”女孩叫道，“我原以为他不会背叛我，而他却早把我忘了。” And when she had lived for a couple of years alone and full of grief, a report was spread over all the land that the King’s daughter was about to celebrate her marriage.The road to the town passed through the village where the maiden was living, and it came to pass that once when the maiden was driving out her herd, her bridegroom travelled by.He was sitting proudly on his horse, and never looked round, but when she saw him she recognized her beloved, and it was just as if a sharp knife had pierced her heart.“Alas!” said she, “I believed him true to me, but he has forgotten me.”
第二天，他再次经过这条路。他走近的时候，女孩对小牛说： Next day he again came along the road.When he was near her she said to the little calf,
“小牛，小牛，跪到我旁边来，不要像王子忘了在酸橙树下等他的未婚妻一样，忘了我这个牧女。” “Little calf, little calf, kneel by my side, And do not forget thy shepherd-maid, As the prince forgot his betrothed bride, Who waited for him ‘neath the lime-tree’s shade.”
王子听到声音，勒住马往下看。他看到了牧女的脸，然后把手放到眼前，好像使劲儿想着什么，不过他马上继续赶路，很快就走远了。“啊！”女孩说道，“他已不再记得我了。”她更加伤心了。 When he was aware of the voice, he looked down and reined in his horse.He looked into the herd’s face, and then put his hands before his eyes as if he were trying to remember something, but he soon rode onwards and was out of sight.“Alas!” said she, “he no longer knows me,” and her grief was ever greater.
没过多久，王宫要举行重大节日庆祝活动，一直持续三天，全国上下每个人都受邀参加。 Soon after this a great festival three days long was to be held at the King’s court, and the whole country was invited to it.
“这是我最后一次机会了。”女孩心想。夜幕降临后，女孩走到埋着宝贝的石头旁。她拿出镶有金太阳的裙子，穿上它，并戴上了珠宝配饰。她把包在发巾下的头发放下来，长长的卷发立刻披散下来，她就这样去了城里，黑夜里谁都没有注意到她。当她走进灯火闪亮的大厅时，人们都惊得目瞪口呆，但是没有人认识她。王子过来接见她，但他还是没有认出来。他邀她跳舞，沉醉于她的美貌，早把新娘忘掉了。盛宴结束后，女孩消失在人群里，拂晓之前赶到了村庄，又换上了放牧女的衣服。 “Now will I try my last chance,” thought the maiden, and when evening came she went to the stone under which she had buried her treasures.She took out the dress with the golden suns, put it on, and adorned herself with the jewels.She let down her hair, which she had concealed under a handkerchief, and it fell down in long curls about her, and thus she went into the town, and in the darkness was observed by no one.When she entered the brightly-lighted hall, every one started back in amazement, but no one knew who she was.The King’s son went to meet her, but he did not recognize her.He led her out to dance, and was so enchanted with her beauty, that he thought no more of the other bride.When the feast was over, she vanished in the crowd, and hastened before daybreak to the village, where she once more put on her herd’s dress.
第二天晚上，她拿出那件件镶着银月亮的裙子，戴上珍宝做的半月形发饰。当她出现在宴会上时，所有人都看着她，王子赶忙走到她身边，对她一见钟情，只跟她跳舞，看都不看其他女孩一眼。走之前，王子要她答应宴会最后一晚一定要来。 Next evening she took out the dress with the silver moons, and put a half-moon made of precious stones in her hair.When she appeared at the festival, all eyes were turned upon her, but the King’s son hastened to meet her, and filled with love for her, danced with her alone, and no longer so much as glanced at anyone else.Before she went away she was forced to promise him to come again to the festival on the last evening.
她第三次出现时，身穿那件星星裙子，每走一步都星光闪烁，发带和裙带上还镶有熠熠发光的珠宝。王子已经等很久了，他情不自禁地走上前来。“请告诉我你是谁，”王子说道，“我觉得跟你似曾相识。”“难道你不知道你离开后我做了什么吗？”女孩迈上台阶，吻了一下王子的左脸，霎时间好像障眼物脱离了他的眼睛，他认出了真正的新娘。“来，”王子对女孩说，“我要离开这里。”他把手伸过去，带她奔向马车。马向魔法城堡飞奔而去，好像风在驾驭着马车一样。他们远远地看到窗户里灯火辉煌。经过酸橙树的时候，无数的萤火虫在树周围飞舞着。酸橙树的树枝摇晃着，散发着阵阵清香。台阶上鲜花盛开，屋里回响着奇异鸟类的歌声，王宫臣仆已经聚集在大厅里，牧师正等着为真正的新郎和新娘完婚。 When she appeared for the third time, she wore the star-dress which sparkled at every step she took, and her hair-ribbon and girdle were starred with jewels.The prince had already been waiting for her for a long time, and forced his way up to her.“Do but tell who thou art,” said he, “I feel just as if I had already known thee a long time.”“Dost thou not know what I did when thou leftest me?”Then she stepped up to him, and kissed him on his left cheek, and in a moment it was as if scales fell from his eyes, and he recognized the true bride.“Come,” said he to her, “here I stay no longer,” gave her his hand, and led her down to the carriage.The horses hurried away to the magic castle as if the wind had been harnessed to the carriage.The illuminated windows already shone in the distance.When they drove past the lime-tree, countless glow-worms were swarming about it.It shook its branches, and sent forth their fragrance.On the steps flowers were blooming, and the room echoed with the song of strange birds, but in the hall the entire court was assembled, and the priest was waiting to marry the bridegroom to the true bride.
兄弟俩 The Two Brothers
从前有一对兄弟，一贫一富。富裕的哥哥是个金匠，心肠歹毒。贫穷的弟弟以扎扫帚为生，为人正直，受人尊重。穷苦的弟弟有一对双胞胎儿子，长得如同两滴水那般相似。两个孩子总去有钱的伯父家串门，偶尔得到些残羹冷炙。碰巧有一次，穷苦的弟弟去森林里砍些柴火，看到一只金色小鸟，美丽得无与伦比。他捡起一块小石头，朝它扔了过去，幸运地打中了，但是只有一根金色羽毛掉了下来，小鸟飞走了。弟弟拿起羽毛，带回去给哥哥看，哥哥看后说：“这是纯金的！”他给了弟弟很多钱，买下了这根羽毛。第二天，弟弟爬上一棵桦树，正要砍树枝，那只小鸟又飞了出来，他仔细寻找，发现了一个鸟巢，里面有个金蛋。他把金蛋带回了家，给哥哥看，哥哥又说道：“这是纯金的。”又给了弟弟很多钱。最后金匠说道：“我要得到那只小鸟。”弟弟第三次去森林里，再次见到了停在树上的金鸟，于是拿起石头把小鸟打了下来，带回去给了哥哥，于是又得到一大堆金子。“现在我有好日子过了。”他心想，然后满足地回家了。 There were once upon a time two brothers, one rich and the other poor.The rich one was a goldsmith and evil-hearted.The poor one supported himself by making brooms, and was good and honourable.The poor one had two children, who were twin brothers and as like each other as two drops of water.The two boys went backwards and forwards to the rich house, and often got some of the scraps to eat.It happened once when the poor man was going into the forest to fetch brush-wood, that he saw a bird which was quite golden and more beautiful than any he had ever chanced to meet with.He picked up a small stone, threw it at him, and was lucky enough to hit him, but one golden feather only fell down, and the bird flew away.The man took the feather and carried it to his brother, who looked at it and said, “It is pure gold!” and gave him a great deal of money for it.Next day the man climbed into a birch-tree, and was about to cut off a couple of branches when the same bird flew out, and when the man searched he found a nest, and an egg lay inside it, which was of gold.He took the egg home with him, and carried it to his brother, who again said, “It is pure gold,” and gave him what it was worth.At last the goldsmith said, “I should indeed like to have the bird itself.”The poor man went into the forest for the third time, and again saw the golden bird sitting on the tree, so he took a stone and brought it down and carried it to his brother, who gave him a great heap of gold for it.“Now I can get on,” thought he, and went contentedly home.
金匠十分狡诈，他很清楚这只鸟的来历。他把妻子叫过来说：“把这只金鸟烤了，注意鸟身上的东西一个都别扔。我想把它全部吃下去。”这只鸟并非凡鸟，它如此地神奇，谁要是吃了它的心和肝，每天早上都会在枕头底下发现一块金子。女人将小鸟收拾好，用烤肉叉子串好，开始烤了起来。金鸟正在火上烤着的时候，因为一些别的活儿，女人不得不离开厨房，这时穷扫帚匠的两个儿子跑了进来，站在烤肉的叉子旁，时不时地把它转动几下。就在这时，鸟上的两小块东西掉到了接油的罐子里，其中一个孩子说：“我们吃掉这两块东西吧，我好饿，没有人会发现的。”然后两个孩子就吃掉了心肝，女人进了厨房发现他们俩在吃东西，问道：“你们在吃什么呢？”“从鸟身上掉下的两小块东西。”他们答道。“一定是心和肝。”女人说道。她非常害怕，为了不让丈夫发现而大发雷霆，她立即杀死了一只小公鸡，取出心和肝，然后放到了金鸟的旁边。烤好后，她把金鸟拿给金匠。他一个人全部吃掉了，一口也不剩。然而，第二天早上，他摸了摸枕头底下，期待着能摸出一块金子，然而却跟往常一样什么都没有。 The goldsmith was crafty and cunning, and knew very well what kind of a bird it was.He called his wife and said, “Roast me the gold bird, and take care that none of it is lost.I have a fancy to eat it all myself.”The bird, however, was no common one, but of so wondrous a kind that whosoever ate its heart and liver found every morning a piece of gold beneath his pillow.The woman made the bird ready, put it on the spit, and let it roast.Now it happened that while it was at the fire, and the woman was forced to go out of the kitchen on account of some other work, the two children of the poor broom-maker ran in, stood by the spit and turned it round once or twice.And as at that very moment two little bits of the bird fell down into the dripping-tin, one of the boys said, “We will eat these two little bits; I am so hungry, and no one will ever miss them.”Then the two ate the pieces, but the woman came into the kitchen and saw that they were eating something and said, “What have ye been eating?”“Two little morsels which fell out of the bird,” answered they.“That must have been the heart and the liver,” said the woman, quite frightened, and in order that her husband might not miss them and be angry, she quickly killed a young cock, took out his heart and liver, and put them beside the golden bird.When it was ready, she carried it to the goldsmith, who consumed it all alone, and left none of it.Next morning, however, when he felt beneath his pillow, and expected to bring out the piece of gold, no more gold pieces were there than there had always been.
两个孩子并不知道他们交了多大的好运。第二天他们醒来时，听到了当啷一声，有东西掉到了地上，他们捡起来，发现竟然是两块金子！他们拿给他们的父亲看，父亲很惊讶，说道：“怎么会有这种事呢？”第二天早上，他们又发现了两块，每天都是如此。他去了哥哥家，告诉了他这个怪事。金匠立刻明白了这是怎么一回事，肯定是两个孩子吃到了金鸟的心和肝。铁石心肠的哥哥非常嫉妒，为了报复，他对孩子的父亲说：“这两个孩子与邪魔王暗中勾结，不要收下那些金子，也不能继续把他们留在家里，因为邪魔王已经掌控了他们，还会毁掉你。”父亲很怕邪魔王，尽管非常痛苦，然而他还是将双胞胎引到森林里，然后悲伤地将他们留在了那里。 The two children did not know what a piece of good-fortune had fallen to their lot.Next morning when they arose, something fell rattling to the ground, and when they picked it up there were two gold pieces!They took them to their father, who was astonished and said, “How can that have happened?”When next morning they again found two, and so on daily, he went to his brother and told him the strange story.The goldsmith at once knew how it had come to pass, and that the children had eaten the heart and liver of the golden bird, and in order to revenge himself, and because he was envious and hard-hearted, he said to the father, “Thy children are in league with the Evil One, do not take the gold, and do not suffer them to stay any longer in thy house, for he has them in his power, and may ruin thee likewise.”The father feared the Evil One, and painful as it was to him, he nevertheless led the twins forth into the forest, and with a sad heart left them there.
现在两个孩子在森林里跑呀跑，寻找回家的路，却总是找不到，只是越走越远。最后他们遇到了一个猎人，猎人问：“你们是谁家的孩子啊？”“我们是穷扫帚匠的儿子。”他们回答道，并告诉他他们的父亲不愿再将他们留在家里，因为每天早上他们的枕头下面都会有一块金子出现。“来吧，”猎人说道：“如果你们诚实，不无所事事，这并不是什么坏事。”好心的猎人很喜欢这两个孩子，自己又没有儿女，便把他们带回了家，说道：“我愿意做你们的父亲，抚养你们长大。”他们跟猎人学习打猎，猎人替他们保存好每天醒来后发现的金子，留着将来派上用场。 And now the two children ran about the forest, and sought the way home again, but could not find it, and only lost themselves more and more.At length they met with a huntsman, who asked, “To whom do you children belong?”“We are the poor broom-maker’s boys,” they replied, and they told him that their father would not keep them any longer in the house because a piece of gold lay every morning under their pillows.“Come,” said the huntsman, “that is nothing so very bad, if at the same time you keep honest, and are not idle.”As the good man liked the children, and had none of his own, he took them home with him and said, “I will be your father, and bring you up till you are big.”They learnt huntsmanship from him, and the piece of gold which each of them found when he awoke, was kept for them by him in case they should need it in the future.
孩子们渐渐长大了。有一天，他们的养父将他们带到森林里，说道：“今天你们要试着打猎了，这样一来你们不必再做学徒，可以成为真正的猎人。”他们跟着他埋伏起来，等了很长时间却依然没有猎物出现。然而猎人抬起头，看到一群大雁呈三角形在天空飞翔。他对其中一个说：“从每个角射下一只。”他照做了，成功完成了试射。一会儿，又有另一群大雁呈“Ｚ”字形飞过。猎人让另外一个孩子从每个角射下一只。同样，他的试射也成功了。“现在，”养父说道，“我宣布你们的学徒期结束，你们成为了合格的猎人。”随即兄弟俩一起走进了森林，相互商量着，好像在计划什么。到了晚上吃晚饭的时候，他们对养父说：“如果你不答应我们的请求，我们就不吃东西，一口都不吃。”养父说：“什么请求呢？”他们答道：“我们已经学会了打猎，我们想去外面的世界证明自己的实力，请让我们去外面见见世面吧。”老人高兴地说：“倒有几分勇敢猎人的风范，你们想得跟我一样，去吧，你们会成功的。”于是他们一起高兴地吃喝起来。 When they were grown up, their foster-father one day took them into the forest with him, and said, “To-day shall you make your trial shot, so that I may release you from your apprenticeship, and make you huntsmen.”They went with him to lie in wait and stayed there a long time, but no game appeared.The huntsman, however, looked above him and saw a covey of wild geese flying in the form of a triangle, and said to one of them, “Shoot me down one from each corner.”He did it, and thus accomplished his trial shot.Soon after another covey came flying by in the form of the figure two, and the huntsman bade the other also bring down one from each corner, and his trial shot was likewise successful.“Now,” said the foster-father, “I pronounce you out of your apprenticeship; you are skilled huntsmen.”Thereupon the two brothers went forth together into the forest, and took counsel with each other and planned something.And in the evening when they had sat down to supper, they said to their foster-father, “We will not touch food, or take one mouthful, until you have granted us a request.”Said he, “What, then, is your request?”They replied, “We have now finished learning, and we must prove ourselves in the world, so allow us to go away and travel.”Then spake the old man joyfully, “You talk like brave huntsmen, that which you desire has been my wish; go forth, all will go well with you.”Thereupon they ate and drank joyously together.
约好的日子来了，养父各送了他们一把好枪和一只狗，并让他们尽量多地带走替他们储存的金块。然后他陪他们走了一段路。离别的时候，他给了他们俩各一把闪闪发亮的刀子，说道：“万一你们哪天分开，将这把刀插在分别地点的一棵树上。当你们其中一个回来的时候，就会知道他的兄弟过得怎么样：如果他死了，那么刀子对着他走的方向的那面会生锈；如果他还活着，那面会依然闪闪发亮。”兄弟俩继续往前走，来到了一片广袤的森林。树林实在太大了，他们不可能一天之内走出去。于是他们在那里过夜，吃着放在袋子里的食物。然而，第二天他们走了一天仍然没走出去。食物吃光了，其中一个说：“我们必须打点东西吃，否则就得挨饿了。”他装上弹药，四处巡视。突然一只老兔子跑上前来，他拿出枪扛在肩膀上，但是兔子喊道： When the appointed day came, their foster-father presented each of them with a good gun and a dog, and let each of them take as many of his saved-up gold pieces as he chose.Then he accompanied them a part of the way, and when taking leave, he gave them a bright knife, and said, “If ever you separate, stick this knife into a tree at the place where you part, and when one of you goes back, he will will be able to see how his absent brother is faring, for the side of the knife which is turned in the direction by which he went, will rust if he dies, but will remain bright as long as he is alive.”The two brothers went still farther onwards, and came to a forest which was so large that it was impossible for them to get out of it in one day.So they passed the night in it, and ate what they had put in their hunting-pouches, but they walked all the second day likewise, and still did not get out.As they had nothing to eat, one of them said, “We must shoot something for ourselves or we shall suffer from hunger,” and loaded his gun, and looked about him.And when an old hare came running up towards them, he laid his gun on his shoulder, but the hare cried,
“亲爱的猎人，放我条生路吧，我会把两只小兔子送给你们。” “Dear huntsman, do but let me live, Two little ones to thee I’ll give,”
它随即钻进了灌木丛，带了两只小兔子出来。但是两个小生灵欢快地玩耍，它们长得非常可爱，猎人不忍心杀掉它们了。于是他们带着两只兔子一起上路，小兔子们蹦蹦跳跳地跟在他们后面。过了一会儿，又爬过一只狐狸，他们正要射杀它，然而狐狸喊道： and sprang instantly into the thicket, and brought two young ones.But the little creatures played so merrily, and were so pretty, that the huntsmen could not find it in their hearts to kill them.They therefore kept them with them, and the little hares followed on foot.Soon after this, a fox crept past; they were just going to shoot it, but the fox cried,
“亲爱的猎人，放我条生路吧，我会把两只小狐狸送给你们。” “Dear hunstman, do but let me live, Two little ones I’ll also give.”
同样它也带了两只小狐狸出来，猎人一只也没杀，而是让它们同兔子做伴，一起跟在后面。没过多久又有一只狼从灌木丛中窜了出来，猎人正端起枪对准了它，然而狼喊道： He, too, brought two little foxes, and the huntsmen did not like to kill them either, but gave them to the hares for company, and they followed behind.It was not long before a wolf strode out of the thicket; the huntsmen made ready to shoot him, but the wolf cried,
“亲爱的猎人，放我条生路吧，我也会把两只小狼送给你。” “Dear huntsman, do but let me live, Two little ones I’ll likewise give.”
猎人把两只小狼也带上了，和其他幼崽一起跟在猎人的身后。然后过来一只熊，也希望不被打死，大声喊道： The huntsmen put the two wolves beside the other animals, and they followed behind them.Then a bear came who wanted to trot about a little longer, and cried:
“亲爱的猎人，放我条生路吧，我也会把两只小熊送给你。” “Dear huntsman, do but let me live, Two little ones I, too, will give.”
又有两只小熊加入了队伍，现在已经有八个成员了。最后谁会来呢？一只狮子走了过来，摇晃着长鬃毛。但是猎人们并不害怕，同样端起枪来，狮子也喊了起来： The two young bears were added to the others, and there were already eight of them.At length who came?A lion came, and tossed his mane.But the huntsmen did not let themselves be frightened and aimed at him likewise, but the lion also said,
“亲爱的猎人，放我条生路吧，我也会把两只小狮子送给你。” “Dear huntsman, do but let me live, Two little ones I, too, will give.”
它给他们带来了两只小狮子。现在，猎人有了两只狮子，两头小熊，两只小狼，两只狐狸，两只兔子跟随着他们，为他们效劳。与此同时，他们的饥饿并没因此而消退，他们对狐狸说：“听着，精明的伙伴，给我们找点吃的去吧。你们又机灵又狡猾。”它们回答道：“不远处有个村庄，我们曾经从那里偷过很多家禽，我俩带你们去。”于是他们去了村庄，买了点吃的，又给小兽们分了一些食物，然后他们继续赶路。两只狐狸非常熟悉这片区域以及家禽禽舍的位置，因而成了猎人的向导。 And he brought his little ones to them, and now the huntsmen had two lions, two bears, two wolves, two foxes, and two hares, who followed them and served them.In thu meantime their hunger was not appeased by this, and they said to the foxes, “Hark ye, cunning fellows, provide us with something to eat.You are crafty and deep.”They replied, “Not far from here lies a village, from which we have already brought many a fowl; we will show you the way there.”So they went into the village, bought themselves something to eat, had some food given to their beasts, and then travelled onwards.The foxes, however, knew their way very well about the district and where the poultry-yards were, and were able to guide the huntsmen.
他们又走了一会儿，但是无法再一起前行了，于是他们说：“没办法了，咱们分道扬镳吧。”他们平分了那些小动物。每个人得到一头狮子，一只小熊，一只狼，一只狐狸和一只兔子。然后他们相互告别，并许下诺言永远像兄弟一样相亲相爱，永世不变。他们把养父送给他们的刀插在一棵树上，然后一个往东，一个往西。 Now they travelled about for a while, but could find no situations where they could remain together, so they said, “There is nothing else for it, we must part.”They divided the animals, so that each of them had a lion, a bear, a wolf, a fox, and a hare, then they took leave of each other, promised to love each other like brothers till their death, and stuck the knife which their foster-father had given them, into a tree, after which one went east, and the other went west.
弟弟带着小动物们到了一个城镇，这里到处飘着黑纱。他走进一家旅店，并询问旅店老板能否留宿动物。旅店老板给了他一间牲口屋，墙上烂了个洞，兔子便溜了出去，偷了空心菜吃，狐狸偷吃了只母鸡，狼吞虎咽吃掉后又逮了只公鸡来吃。但是狼、熊和狮子身躯庞大，无法出去。旅店老板就让人把它们带到了一片草地上，上面正躺着一头牛，它们可以肆无忌惮地享用了。猎人一边照顾小动物们，一边问旅店老板为什么城里到处挂着黑纱。老板说道：“因为我们国王唯一的女儿明天就要死了。”猎人问道：“她难道要病死了吗？”“不是。”老板回答，“她身体很好，然而却必须要死！”“为什么呢？”猎人问道。“城镇外面有座高山，那里住着一条恶龙，每年都要吞食一个纯洁的少女，否则便会让整个国家成为一片废墟。现在，所有的少女都送给他了，只剩下了国王的女儿，但是她也逃不过这一劫，必须要把她交给恶龙，明天就要送去了。”猎人说道：“为什么恶龙没被杀死呢？”“哎，”老板说道，“许多骑士都试过了，但全部牺牲了。国王承诺，谁要是战胜恶龙，就可以娶公主为妻，并可以在他死后继承王位。” The younger, however, arrived with his beasts in a town which was all hung with black crape.He went into an inn, and asked the host if he could accommodate his animals.The innkeeper gave him a stable, where there was a hole in the wall, and the hare crept out and fetched himself the head of a cabbage, and the fox fetched himself a hen, and when he had devoured that got the cock as well, but the wolf, the bear, and the lion could not get out because they were too big.Then the innkeeper let them be taken to a place where a cow was just then lying on the grass, that they might eat till they were satisfied.And when the huntsman had taken care of his animals, he asked the innkeeper why the town was thus hung with black crape?Said the host, “Because our King’s only daughter is to die tomorrow.”The huntsman inquired if she was “sick unto death?”“No,” answered the host, “she is vigorous and healthy, nevertheless she must die!”“How is that?” asked the huntsman.“There is a high hill without the town, whereon dwells a dragon who every year must have a pure virgin, or he lays the whole country waste, and now all the maidens have already been given to him, and there is no longer anyone left but the King’s daughter, yet there is no mercy for her; she must be given up to him, and that is to be done tomorrow.”Said the huntsman, “Why is the dragon not killed?”“Ah,” replied the host, “so many knights have tried it, but it has cost all of them their lives.The King has promised that he who conquers the dragon shall have his daughter to wife, and shall likewise govern the kingdom after his own death.”
猎人没有再多说，但是第二天早上就带上小动物们上了恶龙山。山顶矗立着一个小教堂，祭坛上竖着三支盛满酒的酒杯，上面刻着：“喝掉这三杯酒的人将成为世界上最强壮的人，并将能够挥舞门槛前埋藏的宝剑。”猎人没有喝酒，径直去找地里的宝剑，但却无法挪动它。然后他折了回来，将酒一干而净。现在他充满力量，手臂轻而易举地便拿起了宝剑。将公主交给恶龙的时刻到了。国王、元帅和朝臣陪伴在公主左右。她从远处看到了龙山上的猎人，以为是那只恶龙早已站在上面等她，不想上去。但是最后想到若是不上去，整个城市便要遭受灭顶之灾，于是就被迫踏上了这死亡之路。国王和朝臣回去了，心情极为悲伤。然而，元帅静静伫立着，在远处目睹着一切。 The huntsman said nothing more to this, but next morning took his animals, and with them ascended the dragon’s hill.A little church stood at the top of it, and on the altar three full cups were standing, with the inscription, “Whosoever empties the cups will become the strongest man on earth, and will be able to wield the sword which is buried before the threshold of the door.”The huntsman did not drink, but went out and sought for the sword in the ground, but was unable to move it from its place.Then he went in and emptied the cups, and now he was strong enough to take up the sword, and his hand could quite easily wield it.When the hour came when the maiden was to be delivered over to the dragon, the King, the marshal, and courtiers accompanied her.From afar she saw the huntsman on the dragon’s hill, and thought it was the dragon standing there waiting for her, and did not want to go up to him, but at last, because otherwise the whole town would have been destroyed, she was forced to go the miserable journey.The King and courtiers returned home full of grief; the King’s marshal, however, was to stand still, and see all from a distance.
公主到了山顶之后，在那里等待的并非恶龙，而是年轻的猎人。他安慰公主，并说会救她出去，他带她去了教堂，把她锁在里面。不久，七头龙便从对面咆哮而来。当它意识到猎人的存在时，大吃一惊，说道：“你来山上做什么？”猎人答道：“我来与你决战。”恶龙说道：“许多骑士都在这里丧了命，我也会很快除掉你的。”说着，七张嘴里就一同喷出火来。大火燃起了干草地，猎人原本就要在高温和浓烟里窒息了，然而这时他的小动物们跑了出来，踩灭了大火。恶龙向猎人冲去，他挥舞着宝剑，只听到唰唰几声，猎人砍下了恶龙的三个脑袋。恶龙盛怒，在空中一跃而起，向猎人喷出几道火焰，随即俯身冲下。然而猎人再次拔出宝剑，又砍下了恶龙的三个脑袋。怪兽开始眩晕，快要倒下去了。然而正当它要冲向猎人最后一搏时，猎人用最后一丝气力砍下了恶龙的尾巴。他再也无法战斗了，喊来他的小动物们将恶龙撕成碎片。战斗结束后，猎人打开教堂，公主正躺在地板上。因为刚才决斗时，公主因为痛苦和恐惧晕了过去。他把她抱了出去，她再次苏醒过来，睁开眼睛，他给她看恶龙尸体的碎片，并告诉她她已经获救了。她高兴地说道：“现在你将成为我最爱的丈夫，因为我的父亲承诺将我嫁给杀死恶龙的人。”于是她摘下她的珊瑚项链，分给小动物们作为报答，狮子得到了金扣子。她将上面绣着她名字的手绢送给了猎人，他前去砍掉了恶龙七个头上的舌头，包在手绢里，小心地保存着。 When the King’s daughter got to the top of the hill, it was not the dragon which stood there, but the young huntsman, who comforted her, and said he would save her, led her into the church, and locked her in.It was not long before the seven-headed dragon came thither with loud roaring.When he perceived the huntsman, he was astonished and said, “What business hast thou here on the hill?”The huntsman answered, “I want to fight with thee.”Said the dragon, “Many knights have left their lives here, I shall soon have made an end of thee too,” and he breathed fire out of seven jaws.The fire was to have lighted the dry grass, and the huntsman was to have been suffocated in the heat and smoke, but the animals came running up and trampled out the fire.Then the dragon rushed upon the huntsman, but he swung his sword until it sang through the air, and struck off three of his heads.Then the dragon grew right furious, and rose up in the air, and spat out flames of fire over the huntsman, and was about to plunge down on him, but the huntsman once more drew out his sword, and again cut off three of his heads.The monster became faint and sank down, nevertheless it was just able to rush upon the huntsman, but he with his last strength smote its tail off, and as he could fight no longer, called up his animals who tore it in pieces.When the struggle was ended, the huntsman unlocked the church, and found the King’s daughter lying on the floor, as she had lost her senses with anguish and terror during the contest.He carried her out, and when she came to herself once more, and opened her eyes, he showed her the dragon all cut to pieces, and told her that she was now delivered.She rejoiced and said, “Now thou wilt be my dearest husband, for my father has promised me to him who kills the dragon.”Thereupon she took off her necklace of coral, and divided it amongst the animals in order to reward them, and the lion received the golden clasp.Her pocket-handkerchief, however, on which was her name, she gave to the huntsman, who went and cut the tongues out of the dragon’s seven heads, wrapped them in the handkerchief, and preserved them carefully.
包好之后，猎人感到全身无力，经历了大火和战斗的他非常疲惫，他对公主说：“我们都很累了，睡一会儿吧。”公主说：“好的。”于是他们躺在了地上，猎人对狮子说：“你要好好看守，防止有人惊动我们。”两个人便睡着了。狮子卧在他们身边，但是它也累得够呛，于是把小熊叫了过来，说道：“卧在我旁边吧，我得睡会儿，如果有什么事就叫醒我。”然后小熊在它身边卧下身来，但是它也累了，于是把狼叫过来说：“卧在我旁边吧，我得睡会儿，如果有事就叫醒我。”然后狼在它身边卧下身来，但是它同样很累，就叫来狐狸对它说：“卧在我旁边吧，我得睡会儿，如果有事就叫醒我。”然后狐狸就在它身旁卧下身来，但是它也很累，就叫来兔子对它说：“卧在我旁边吧，我得睡会儿，如果有事就叫醒我。”然后兔子在它身旁坐下，但是可怜的兔子也累了，却找不到人继续看守，也睡着了。现在公主、猎人、狮子、小熊、狼、狐狸和兔子都在熟睡中。然而，元帅从远处看着山上，等到看不见带着公主飞舞的恶龙时便壮起胆子，趁着山里一片寂静的时候，偷偷上了山。山上残留着恶龙被砍成的碎片，不远处躺着公主和猎人，还有他的小动物们，他们全都沉沉睡去了。歹毒的元帅挥剑砍掉了猎人的脑袋，将公主一把抓进怀中，带着她下山了。公主醒来时被吓到了，但是元帅说道：“你在我的手里，你要说是我杀死了恶龙。”“我不能这么做。”她回答道，“是猎人和他的小动物们杀死了恶龙。”然后他拔出宝剑，并威胁如果她不顺从就杀了她，于是公主被迫同意了。元帅带着公主去见国王。看到亲爱的孩子还活着，国王抑制不住自己的喜悦，他原本以为公主已经被恶龙撕成了碎片。元帅对他说：“我杀死了恶龙，拯救了公主和整个王国，因此我要求公主做我的妻子，正如之前所承诺的那样。”国王问公主：“他说的是真的吗？”“嗯，是的。”公主回答道，“这当然是真的，但是我希望在一年零一天之后举行婚礼。”因为她想这段时间内她也许能打探到猎人的消息。 That done, as he was so faint and weary with the fire and the battle, he said to the maiden, “We are both faint and weary, we will sleep awhile.”Then she said, “yes,” and they lay down on the ground, and the huntsman said to the lion, “Thou shalt keep watch, that no one surprises us in our sleep,” and both fell asleep.The lion lay down beside them to watch, but he also was so weary with the fight, that he called to the bear and said, “Lie down near me, I must sleep a little: if anything comes, waken me.”Then the bear lay down beside him, but he also was tired, and called the wolf and said, “Lie down by me, I must sleep a little, but if anything comes, waken me.”Then the wolf lay down by him, but he was tired likewise, and called the fox and said, “Lie down by me, I must sleep a little; if anything comes, waken me.”Then the fox lay down beside him, but he too was weary, and called the hare and said, “Lie down near me, I must sleep a little, and if anything should come, waken me.”Then the hare sat down by him, but the poor hare was tired too, and had no one whom he could call there to keep watch, and fell asleep.And now the King’s daughter, the huntsman, the lion, the bear, the wolf, the fox, and the hare, were all sleeping a sound sleep.The marshal, however, who was to look on from a distance, took courage when he did not see the dragon flying away with the maiden, and finding that all the hill had become quiet, ascended it.There lay the dragon hacked and hewn to pieces on the ground, and not far from it were the King’s daughter and a huntsman with his animals, and all of them were sunk in a sound sleep.And as he was wicked and godless he took his sword, cut off the huntsman’s head, and seized the maiden in his arms, and carried her down the hill.Then she awoke and was terrified, but the marshal said, “Thou art in my hands, thou shalt say that it was I who killed the dragon.”“I cannot do that,” she replied, “for it was a huntsman with his animals who did it.”Then he drew his sword, and threatened to kill her if she did not obey him, and so compelled her that she promised it.Then he took her to the King, who did not know how to contain himself for joy when he once more looked on his dear child in life, whom he had believed to have been torn to pieces by the monster.The marshal said to him, “I have killed the dragon, and delivered the maiden and the whole kingdom as well, therefore I demand her as my wife, as was promised.”The King said to the maiden, “Is what he says true?”“Ah, yes,” she answered, “it must indeed be true, but I will not consent to have the wedding celebrated until after a year and a day,” for she thought in that time she should hear something of her dear huntsman.
然而，恶龙山上，小动物们依然在它们死去的主人身边酣睡着。一只大黄蜂飞到兔子的鼻子上，兔子用爪子把它赶走了，接着又睡着了。大黄蜂又来了，兔子依然赶走了它，继续睡觉。然后第三次大黄蜂又来了，在兔子的鼻子上蛰了一口，这下兔子醒了。兔子醒后，立即叫醒了狐狸，狐狸叫醒了狼，狼叫醒了熊，最后熊叫醒了狮子。狮子醒来后发现公主不见了，主人也死了，它开始疯狂地咆哮，哭喊着：“这是谁干的？熊，你为什么不叫醒我？”熊接着问狼：“你为什么不叫醒我？”狼问狐狸：“你为什么不叫醒我？”狐狸问兔子：“你为什么不叫醒我？”唯有可怜的兔子不知该怎样回答，矛头便指向了它。它们正要一怒而起，兔子恳求它们说：“不要杀我，我会让主人重新活过来的。我知道一座山，上面生长着一种仙草，不管将它放到谁的嘴巴里，皆可治愈所有的疾病和每一处创伤。但是山离这里有两百个小时的路程。”狮子说：“在二十四小时内，你必须到达那里，摘到仙草然后返回。”然后兔子狂奔开来，二十四小时内果然回来了，身上带着仙草。狮子把猎人的头和身子对好，兔子将仙草放进他的嘴里，伤口随即愈合了，他有了脉搏，重新活了过来。后来猎人醒了，发现公主不在非常吃惊，心想：“为了躲开我，她一定是在我睡觉的时候走掉了。”狮子在匆忙之中把主人的脑袋接反了，但是猎人仍沉溺在失去公主的悲伤之中，并没有发觉。但是中午吃饭的时候，他发现脑袋朝着后面，感到不可理解，便问小动物们睡觉的时候发生过什么。然后狮子告诉他，它们也因为疲惫而睡着了，醒来时发现他的头被砍掉了，兔子带回了回生草，而它在匆忙之中把他的脑袋接反了，但是它将改正它的过错。然后它又拔掉猎人的脑袋，转过来之后，兔子给他吃了仙草，伤口便愈合了。 The animals, however, were still lying sleeping beside their dead master on the dragon’s hill, and there came a great humble-bee and lighted on the hare’s nose, but the hare wiped it off with his paw, and went on sleeping.The humble-bee came a second time, but the hare again rubbed it off and slept on.Then it came for the third time, and stung his nose so that he awoke.As soon as the hare was awake, he roused the fox, and the fox, the wolf, and the wolf the bear, and the bear the lion.And when the lion awoke and saw that the maiden was gone, and his master was dead, he began to roar frightfully and cried, “Who has done that?Bear, why didst thou not waken me?”The bear asked the wolf, “Why didst thou not waken me?” and the wolf the fox, “Why didst thou not waken me?” and the fox the hare, “Why didst thou not waken me?”The poor hare alone did not know what answer to make, and the blame rested with him.Then they were just going to fall upon him, but he entreated them and said, “Kill me not, I will bring our master to life again.I know a mountain on which a root grows which, when placed in the mouth of any one, cures him of all illness and every wound.But the mountain lies two hundred hours journey from here.”The lion said, “In four-and-twenty hours must thou have run thither and have come back, and have brought the root with thee.”Then the hare sprang away, and in four-and-twenty hours he was back, and brought the root with him.The lion put the huntsman’s head on again, and the hare placed the root in his mouth, and immediately everything united together again, and his heart beat, and life came back.Then the huntsman awoke, and was alarmed when he did not see the maiden, and thought, “She must have gone away whilst I was sleeping, in order to get rid of me.”The lion in his great haste had put his master’s head on the wrong way round, but the huntsman did not observe it because of his melancholy thoughts about the King’s daughter.But at noon, when he was going to eat something, he saw that his head was turned backwards and could not understand it, and asked the animals what had happened to him in his sleep.Then the lion told him that they, too, had all fallen asleep from weariness, and on awaking, had found him dead with his head cut off, that the hare had brought the life-giving root, and that he, in his haste, had laid hold of the head the wrong way, but that he would repair his mistake.Then he tore the huntsman’s head off again, turned it round, and the hare healed it with the root.
然而猎人却心伤难愈，他周游世界，领着动物们给人们表演舞蹈。就在一年的年末他又回到了当年从恶龙手里解救公主的那个城市，这次这里到处挂着喜庆的红布。然后他问老板说：“这是什么意思呢？去年整个城市都挂着黑纱，今天的红布是什么意思呢？”店主回答道：“去年公主本来就要落到恶龙手里了，所以挂着黑纱。然而元帅与恶龙奋战，杀死了它，明天他们将正式举行婚礼，所以挂上了喜庆的红布。” The huntsman, however, was sad at heart, and travelled about the world, and made his animals dance before people.It came to pass that precisely at the end of one year he came back to the same town where he had delivered the King’s daughter from the dragon, and this time the town was gaily hung with red cloth.Then he said to the host, “What does this mean?Last year the town was all hung with black crape, what means the red cloth to-day?”The host answered, “Last year our King’s daughter was to have been delivered over to the dragon, but the marshal fought with it and killed it, and so to-morrow their wedding is to be solemnized, and that is why the town was then hung with black crape for mourning, and is to-day covered with red cloth for joy?”
第二天即将举行婚礼，中午时分猎人对旅店老板说：“你信不信，老板，我们俩今天坐在这儿就能吃到国王餐桌上的面包？”“不可能的，”老板说，“我用一百块金子做赌注，你说的不会实现。”猎人接受这个赌注，也拿出了一个钱包，里面放着同样多的金子。然后他把兔子叫过来说：“去吧，亲爱的跑步健将，帮我取些国王正吃的面包来。”小兔子是动物中地位最低的一个，无法将命令转交予其他伙伴，只能自己去了。“啊！”兔子想到，“如果我独自穿过大街，屠户家的狗肯定会追我的。”正如它所料，几只狗追着它，想把它的皮剥下来。但是兔子蹦蹦跳跳地跑开了。难道你没看见它跑过去么？它趁着士兵不注意，溜进了一个岗亭里。然后狗跑了过来，想让兔子出来，但是士兵并不明白发生了什么，用枪托对着它们一通好打，狗叫喊着跑开了。兔子一看外面安全了，便向王宫跑去，径直跑到了公主身边，它在她的椅子下面坐下来，挠她的脚丫。然后她说：“到一边去。”公主以为是她的狗。兔子又挠了挠她的脚丫，她又说道：“到一边去。”以为又是她的狗。兔子并没有放弃，于是第三次挠公主的脚丫。公主往下瞄了眼，看到了它的项圈，知道原来是兔子。她把它抱起来，带进了她的房间，说道：“亲爱的兔子，你在这里做什么呢？”它答道：“我那杀死恶龙的主人在这个城市，他派我来要一片国王吃的面包。”公主很高兴，唤来面包师，命令他拿来一片国王吃的那种面包。小兔子说道：“但是面包师必须还要帮我送到那里，这样一来屠夫的狗就不会伤害我了。”面包师一直送到旅店门口，然后兔子后腿蹬直，用前爪取来面包，送给了猎人。然后猎人说：“看，老板，这一百块金子是我的了。”老板大吃一惊，但是猎人继续说道：“是的，老板，我有了面包，但现在我还想要国王的烤肉。” Next day when the wedding was to take place, the huntsman said at mid-day to the inn-keeper, “Do you believe, sir host, that I while with you here to-day shall eat bread from the King’s own table?”“Nay,” said the host, “I would bet a hundred pieces of gold that that will not come true.”The huntsman accepted the wager, and set against it a purse with just the same number of gold pieces.Then he called the hare and said, “Go, my dear runner, and fetch me some of the bread which the King is eating.”Now the little hare was the lowest of the animals, and could not transfer this order to any the others, but had to get on his legs himself.“Alas!” thought he, “if I bound through the streets thus alone, the butchers’ dogs will all be after me.”It happened as he expected, and the dogs came after him and wanted to make holes in his good skin.But he sprang away, have you have never seen one running?and sheltered himself in a sentry-box without the soldier being aware of it.Then the dogs came and wanted to have him out, but the soldier did not understand a jest, and struck them with the butt-end of his gun, till they ran away yelling and howling.As soon as the hare saw that
