the way was clear, he ran into the palace and straight to the King’s daughter, sat down under her chair, and scratched at her foot.Then she said, “Wilt thou get away?” and thought it was her dog.The hare scratched her foot for the second time, and she again said, “Wilt thou get away?” and thought it was her dog.But the hare did not let itself be turned from its purpose, and scratched her for the third time.Then she peeped down, and knew the hare by its collar.She took him on her lap, carried him into her chamber, and said, “Dear Hare, what dost thou want?”He answered, “My master, who killed the dragon, is here, and has sent me to ask for a loaf of bread like that which the King eats.”Then she was full of joy and had the baker summoned, and ordered him to bring a loaf such as was eaten by the King.The little hare said, “But the baker must likewise carry it thither for me, that the butchers’ dogs may do no harm to me.”The baker carried it for him as far as the door of the inn, and then the hare got on his hind legs, took the loaf in his front paws, and carried it to his master.Then said the huntsman, “Behold, sir host, the hundred pieces of gold are mine.”The host was astonished, but the huntsman went on to say, “Yes, sir host, I have the bread, but now I will likewise have some of the King’s roast meat.”
老板说道：“我倒想看看。”但他不愿意再下赌注了。猎人叫来狐狸说道：“我的小狐狸，去帮我取些烤肉来，就跟国王吃的一样。”红狐狸非常聪明，它借着边边角角，没有让狗看到它，也坐在了公主的椅子下面，挠她的脚丫。公主往下看，认出了狐狸的项圈，她带它进了房间，说道：“亲爱的狐狸，你在这里做什么呢？”它答道：“我那杀掉恶龙的主人在这个城市，他派我来的。我来要些国王吃的那种烤肉。”然后她把厨师叫来，命令他准备一份跟国王吃的一样的烤肉，并替狐狸送到旅店门口。然后狐狸接过盘子，摇了摇尾巴，赶走了落在肉上的苍蝇，送到了主人那里。“看，老板，”猎人说道，“现在面包和烤肉都有了，现在我还想搭配点蔬菜，就像国王吃的那种。”然后他叫来了狼，对它说：“亲爱的狼，去帮我取些蔬菜过来，就跟国王吃的一样。”然后狼直奔王宫，因为它无所畏惧，到了公主身边，它从后面扯公主的裙子，公主便要回头看。她认出了它的项圈，带她去房间，问道：“亲爱的狼，你想要什么呢？”它答道：“我那杀死恶龙的主人在这个城里，我想要些蔬菜，就跟国王吃的一样。”然后她喊来厨师，叫他准备了一盘蔬菜，跟国王吃的一样，还要帮狼送到旅店门口，然后狼接过盘子，献给了主人。“看，老板，”猎人说道，“现在我有了面包，烤肉和蔬菜，我还想要糕点，跟国王吃的一样。”他唤来熊，对它说：“亲爱的熊，你喜欢舔甜的东西，去帮我带些糖果回来，就像国王吃的一样。”然后熊跑着去了王宫，每个人都给它让路，但遇到了卫兵，他们却持枪拦住了它。但是熊蹬起后腿，用爪子给了他们几个大耳光，然后卫兵纷纷倒下了，它直奔公主，藏在公主后面，小声地叫着。公主往后看，认出了熊，招呼它去公主的房间，说道：“亲爱的熊，你想要什么呢？”它答道：“我那杀死恶龙的主人在这个城里，我想要些糖果，就像国王吃的那种。”然后她唤来糖果师傅，命令他准备一份国王吃的那种糖果，还帮熊送到了旅店门口。熊先把掉下的糖果舔干净，然后站直了，结果盘子，献给了主人。“看吧，老板，”猎人说，“我现在有了面包、烤肉、蔬菜和糖果，我还想喝几杯，就跟国王喝的一样。”他唤来狮子，对他说：“亲爱的狮子，你自己总爱喝几杯，去帮我取些酒来吧，就跟国王喝的一样。”然后狮子大摇大摆地上街了，人们避之唯恐不及，遇到了门卫，他们想要拦着它。它随即大吼一声，门卫们全部落荒而逃。狮子去了王宫，用尾巴敲了敲门。然后公主走上前来，被狮子吓了一跳，但她认出了她的金扣子，便招呼它来自己的房间，对它说：“亲爱的狮子，你想要什么呢？”他答道：“我那杀死恶龙的主人在这座城里，我想要些好酒，就是国王喝的那种。”然后她唤来侍酒者，让他为狮子准备些国王喝的那种酒来。狮子说道：“我想同他去，以确保他不会弄错。”然后它跟着侍酒者下去了，到了下面之后，他想给狮子取些国王仆人喝的普通酒，但是狮子说道：“住手，先让我来尝一下。”它一口便吞下了半瓶。“不，”它说，“不是这种。”侍酒者白了它一眼，接着正要从另一个瓶子里取些元帅喝的酒。狮子说道：“住手，先让我来尝一尝。”便又喝掉半瓶。“这个好一些，但还不是。”它说道。侍酒者生气地说道：“你这种蠢狮子怎么会懂呢？”狮子在他脑袋后边猛地一击，侍酒者重重地摔在了地上。爬起来后，他默默地领着狮子进了一个小酒窖，这里放着国王的酒，别人从未喝过。狮子上去把半瓶喝掉了，说这才像是国王的酒，然后命令调酒师把六个瓶子都装得满满的。现在他们又上楼去了，但是狮子一从酒窖走到外面，便左摇右晃，醉意浓浓了。侍酒者不得不替它把酒送到旅店门口，然后狮子用嘴巴叼着篮子把，给主人送去了。猎人说：“看吧，老板，我有了面包、烤肉、蔬菜、糖果、美酒，就跟国王的盛宴一样，现在我要跟我的小动物们一同进餐了。”他坐下来，把吃的喝的分给小动物们。他兴高采烈，因为他知道公主还是爱着他的。吃完晚饭后，他说：“老板，国王的饭菜和美酒我已经享用过了，现在我要去王宫里迎娶公主。”老板说：“怎么可能，公主已经订婚了，婚礼就在今天举行。”然后猎人拿出了公主在恶龙山上送他的手绢，里面包着怪兽的七个舌头，猎人说：“我手里的东西将助我一臂之力。”旅店老板看了看手绢说：“我就是什么都信也不会相信这个的，我愿意拿我的房子和院子作为赌注。”然而猎人却掏出装有一千块金子的钱袋，放到桌上说：“这是我的赌注。” The host said, “I should indeed like to see that,” but he would make no more wagers.The huntsman called the fox and said, “My little fox, go and fetch me some roast meat, such as the King eats.”The red fox knew the bye-ways better, and went by holes and corners without any dog seeing him, seated himself under the chair of the King’s daughter, and scratched her foot.Then she looked down and recognized the fox by its collar, took him into her chamber with her and said, “Dear fox, what dost thou want?”He answered, “My master, who killed the dragon, is here, and has sent me.I am to ask for some roast meat such as the King is eating.”Then she made the cook come, who was obliged to prepare a roast joint, the same as was eaten by the King, and to carry it for the fox as far as the door.Then the fox took the dish, waved away with his tail the flies which had settled on the meat, and then carried it to his master.“Behold, sir host,” said the huntsman, “bread and meat are here but now I will also have proper vegetables with it, such as are eaten by the King.”Then he called the wolf, and said, “Dear Wolf, go thither and fetch me vegetables such as the King eats.”Then the wolf went straight to the palace, as he feared no one, and when he got to the King’s daughter’s chamber, he twitched at the back of her dress, so that she was forced to look round.She recognized him by his collar, and took him into her chamber with her, and said, “Dear Wolf, what dost thou want?”He answered, “My master, who killed the dragon, is here, I am to ask for some vegetables, such as the King eats.”Then she made the cook come, and he had to make ready a dish of vegetables, such as the King ate, and had to carry it for the wolf as far as the door, and then the wolf took the dish from him, and carried it to his master.“Behold, sir host,” said the huntsman, “now I have bread and meat and vegetables, but I will also have some pastry to eat like that which the King eats.”He called the bear, and said, “Dear Bear, thou art fond of licking anything sweet; go and bring me some confectionery, such as the King eats.”Then the bear trotted to the palace, and every one got out of his way, but when he went to the guard, they presented their muskets, and would not let him go into the royal palace.But he got up on his hind legs, and gave them a few boxes on the ears, right and left, with his paws, so that the whole watch broke up, and then he went straight to the King’s daughter, placed himself behind her, and growled a little.Then she looked behind her, knew the bear, and bade him go into her room with her, and said, “Dear Bear, what dost thou want?”He answered, “My master, who killed the dragon, is here, and I am to ask for some confectionery, such as the King eats.”Then she summoned her confectioner, who had to bake confectionery such as the King ate, and carry it to the door for the bear; then the bear first licked up the comfits which had rolled down, and then he stood upright, took the dish, and carried it to his master.“Behold, sir host,” said the huntsman, “now I have bread, meat, vegetables and confectionery, but I will drink wine also, and such as the King drinks.”He called his lion to him and said, “Dear Lion, thou thyself likest to drink till thou art intoxicated, go and fetch me some wine, such as is drunk by the King.”Then the lion strode through the streets, and the people fled from him, and when he came to the watch, they wanted to bar the way against him, but he did but roar once, and they all ran away.Then the lion went to the royal apartment, and knocked at the door with his tail.Then the King’s daughter came forth, and was almost afraid of the lion, but she knew him by the golden clasp of her necklace, and bade him go with her into her chamber, and said, “Dear Lion, what wilt thou have?”He answered, “My master, who killed the dragon, is here, and I am to ask for some wine such as is drunk by the King.”Then she bade the cup-bearer be called, who was to give the lion some wine like that which was drunk by the King.The lion said, “I will go with him, and see that I get the right wine.”Then he went down with the cup-bearer, and when they were below, the cup-bearer wanted to draw him some of the common wine that was drunk by the King’s servants, but the lion said, “Stop, I will taste the wine first,” and he drew half a measure, and swallowed it down at one draught.“No,” said he, “that is not right.”The cup-bearer looked at him askance, but went on, and was about to give him some out of another barrel which was for the King’s marshal.The lion said, “Stop, let me taste the wine first,” and drew half a measure and drank it.“That is better, but still not right,” said he.Then the cup-bearer grew angry and said, “How can a stupid animal like you understand wine?”But the lion gave him a blow behind the ears, which made him fall down by no means gently, and when he had got up again, he conducted the lion quite silently into a little cellar apart, where the King’s wine lay, from which no one ever drank.The lion first drew half a measure and tried the wine, and then he said, That may possibly be the right sort, and bade the cup-bearer fill six bottles of it.And now they went upstairs again, but when the lion came out of the cellar into the open air, he reeled here and there, and was rather drunk, and the cup-bearer was forced to carry the wine as far as the door for him, and then the lion took the handle of the basket in his mouth, and took it to his master.The huntsman said, “Behold, sir host, here have I bread, meat, vegetables, confectionery and wine such as the King has, and now I will dine with my animals,” and he sat down and ate and drank, and gave the hare, the fox, the wolf, the bear, and the lion also to eat and to drink, and was joyful, for he saw that the King’s daughter still loved him.And when he had finished his dinner, he said, “Sir host, now have I eaten and drunk, as the King eats and drinks, and now I will go to the King’s court and marry the King’s daughter.”Said the host, “How can that be, when she already has a betrothed husband, and when the wedding is to be solemnized today?”Then the huntsman drew forth the handkerchief which the King’s daughter had given him on the dragon’s hill, and in which were folded the monster’s seven tongues, and said, “That which I hold in my hand shall help me to do it.”Then the innkeeper looked at the handkerchief, and said, “Whatever I believe, I do not believe that, and I am willing to stake my house and courtyard on it.”The huntsman, however, took a bag with a thousand gold pieces, put it on the table, and said, “I stake that on it.”
用膳时国王问公主：“那些动物在王宫里进进出出，它们来找你干嘛呢？”她答道：“我不敢告诉您，但是如果您接见它们的主人，那上天一定会保佑您的。”国王派人去了旅店邀请猎人，正当猎人刚跟老板打赌，仆人便进来了。他说：“看吧，老板，国王派仆人来接我了，但我不会这样去的。”他对仆人说：“我请求国王陛下送我一套王衣、一辆六套马车和奴仆前来迎接我。”国王听到答复后问公主：“我该怎么办呢？”公主说：“就按照他说的做吧，上天会保佑您的。”于是国王让人送去了王服，一辆六套马车和仆人，等着迎接他。看到他们来了，猎人说：“看吧，老板，我要如愿以偿地出发了。”他穿上王服，拿着裹着龙舌的手绢，乘着马车去王宫了。国王看到他来了，问公主：“我该怎么接待他呢？”公主回答：“亲自接见他吧，上天会保佑您的。”然后国王前去接见他，让他进来，他的小动物们也跟着进来了。国王让他在自己和公主旁边就座。元帅，也就是新郎，坐在对面，但却认不出猎人了。就在这时，恶龙的七个首级献了上来，国王说：“这七个首级是元帅从恶龙身上砍下来的，因此今天我要将公主嫁给他。”猎人站了起来，打开七个首级的嘴巴，说道：“恶龙的七个舌头去哪了呢？”元帅吓得不知所措，脸色煞白，不知该怎样回答，最后他极为痛苦地狡辩道：“恶龙没有舌头。”猎人说：“说谎的人才没有舌头，而恶龙的舌头正是杀死恶龙的证据。”说着便打开了手绢，七个舌头全在里面。他逐个放到原先的嘴巴里，正好合适。然后他拿起绣着公主名字的手绢给公主看，并问当年把它赠与了谁，公主回答：“是杀掉恶龙的勇士。”然后他喊来了他的小动物们，从他们身上取下项圈和狮子戴的金扣子，拿给公主看并问这是属于谁的。她答道：“项链和金扣子都是我的，但是我把它们分给了帮助勇士杀掉恶龙的小动物们。”然后猎人说：“当时我精疲力尽，而元帅趁我睡觉的时候上山砍掉了我的头。然后他便挟着公主下山了，并宣布是他杀掉了恶龙，但是我用恶龙的舌头、公主的手绢和项链证明了他的谎言。”然后他讲述了他的小动物们如何用一种仙草将他救活，以及过去的一年里如何带着小动物们到处流浪，最后终于又回到了这个城里，并从旅店老板那里得知了元帅的阴谋。然后国王问公主：“真的是他杀掉了恶龙吗？”公主回答：“是的，的确如此。现在真相大白了，我终于可以揭露元帅的罪行了，因为就是他威胁我不让我说出去。正因如此，我才提出来要在一年零一天之后举行婚礼。”然后国王召见了十二位王公大臣，对元帅宣判。他们判决元帅要被四头公牛撕成碎片。因而元帅被处决了，而国王将女儿许配给了猎人，并任命他为国家总督。大家欢快隆重地庆祝公主和猎人的婚礼，年轻的国王请来了他的父亲和养父，并送给他们大堆的金银财宝。他也没有忘记旅店老板，而是将他请来，说道：“看吧，老板，我已经迎娶了公主，你的房子和院子都是我的了。”老板说道：“是的，理应如此。”但是年轻的国王说：“我要好好犒劳你。”然后告诉他房子和院子还是他的，还送给他一千块金子。 Now the King said to his daughter, at the royal table, “What did all the wild animals want, which have been coming to thee, and going in and out of my palace?”She replied, “I may not tell you, but send and have the master of these animals brought, and you will do well.”The King sent a servant to the inn, and invited the stranger, and the servant came just as the huntsman had laid his wager with the innkeeper.Then said he, “Behold, sir host, now the King sends his servant and invites me, but I do not go in this way.”And he said to the servant, “I request the Lord King to send me royal clothing, and a carriage with six horses, and servants to attend me.”When the King heard the answer, he said to his daughter, “What shall I do?”She said, “Cause him to be fetched as he desires to be, and you will do well.”Then the King sent royal apparel, a carriage with six horses, and servants to wait on him.When the huntsman saw them coming, he said, “Behold, sir host, now I am fetched as I desired to be,” and he put on the royal garments, took the handkerchief with the dragon’s tongues with him, and drove off to the King.When the King saw him coming, he said to his daughter, “How shall I receive him?”She answered, “Go to meet him and you will do well.”Then the King went to meet him and led him in, and his animals followed.The King gave him a seat near himself and his daughter, and the marshal, as bridegroom, sat on the other side, but no longer knew the huntsman.And now at this very moment, the seven heads of the dragon were brought in as a spectacle, and the King said, “The seven heads were cut off the dragon by the marshal, wherefore to-day I give him my daughter to wife.”The the huntsman stood up, opened the seven mouths, and said, “Where are the seven tongues of the dragon?”Then was the marshal terrified, and grew pale and knew not what answer he should make, and at length in his anguish he said, “Dragons have no tongues.”The huntsman said, “Liars ought to have none, but the dragon’s tongues are the tokens of the victor,” and he unfolded the handkerchief, and there lay all seven inside it.And he put each tongue in the mouth to which it belonged, and it fitted exactly.Then he took the handkerchief on which the name of the princess was embroidered, and showed it to the maiden, and asked to whom she had given it, and she replied, “To him who killed the dragon.”And then he called his animals, and took the collar off each of them and the golden clasp from the lion, and showed them to the maiden and asked to whom they belonged.She answered, “The necklace and golden clasp were mine, but I divided them among the animals who helped to conquer the dragon.”Then spake the huntsman, “When I, tired with the fight, was resting and sleeping, the marshal came and cut off my head.Then he carried away the King’s daughter, and gave out that it was he who had killed the dragon, but that he lied I prove with the tongues, the handkerchief, and the necklace.”And then he related how his animals had healed him by means of a wonderful root, and how he had travelled about with them for one year, and had at length again come there and had learnt the treachery of the marshal by the inn-keeper’s story.Then the King asked his daughter, “Is it true that this man killed the dragon?”And she answered, “Yes, it is true.Now can I reveal the wicked deed of the marshal, as it has come to light without my connivance, for he wrung from me a promise to be silent.For this reason, however, did I make the condition that the marriage should not be solemnized for a year and a day.”Then the King bade twelve councillors be summoned who were to pronounce judgment on the marshal, and they sentenced him to be torn to pieces by four bulls.The marshal was therefore executed, but the King gave his daughter to the huntsman, and named him his viceroy over the whole kingdom.The wedding was celebrated with great joy, and the young King caused his father and his foster-father to be brought, and loaded them with treasures.Neither did he forget the inn-keeper, but sent for him and said, “Behold, sir host, I have married the King’s daughter, and your house and yard are mine.”The host said, “Yes, according to justice it is so.”But the young King said, “It shall be done according to mercy,” and told him that he should keep his house and yard, and gave him the thousand pieces of gold as well.
现在年轻的国王和王后幸福美满地生活着。他经常外出打猎，这是他的爱好，忠心的小动物们也总会陪着他。然而附近有个森林，相传那里鬼魂出没，不论谁进去便很难再出来了。然而，年轻的国王很想去那里打猎，老国王一天不让他去，他便一天不得安宁。于是他带着大队人马出发了。到了森林里，他看到一头雪白的雄鹿，对他的随从说：“在这里等我回来，我想去追赶这个美丽的生灵。”于是他驾着马追赶雄鹿，只有他的小动物跟在后面。随从们一直等到了晚上，但是他还没有回来，于是他们便回去告诉年轻的王后，年轻的国王去森林追赶一头白色雄鹿，还没有回来。她担心起来。然而他还不停地追赶着这只美丽的小兽，但却始终追不上。每当他感觉快要接近目标了，便看到它又随即跑远了，最后一溜烟不见了。现在他发现已经身处森林深处，他吹响号角却没有回音，因为随从们早就听不见了。夜幕降临，他知道今天肯定回不去了，于是下了马，在一棵树旁生起火，决定在这里过夜。他在火边坐着，小动物们也在他身边卧下来，这时他好像听到了人的声音。他看了看四周，什么都没发现。不一会儿，他又听到了呻吟声，好像是从上面传来的，他抬头看，看到一个老妇人坐在树上，不停地哭着：“啊，好冷啊！”猎人说：“下来吧，冷的话就在这里暖和一会儿。”但是她说：“不，这些动物会咬我的。”他答道：“他们不会伤害你的，老婆婆，请下来吧。”谁知道她竟然是个巫婆，她说道：“我会从树上扔一根树枝下去，如果你用树枝抽打它们的后背，它们就不会伤害我。”然后她扔给他一根小树枝。他照做了，小动物们随即一动不动，全部变成了石头。女巫安全了，她从树上跳下来，用树枝将他一点，也把他变成了石头。于是她哈哈大笑，把他和小动物们拖进了一个大坑，那里已经放了好多这样的石头。 And now the young King and Queen were thoroughly happy, and lived in gladness together.He often went out hunting because it was a delight to him, and the faithful animals had to accompany him.In the neighborhood, however, there was a forest of which it was reported that it was haunted, and that whosoever did but enter it did not easily get out again.The young King, however, had a great inclination to hunt in it, and let the old King have no peace until he allowed him to do so.So he rode forth with a great following, and when he came to the forest, he saw a snow-white hart and said to his people, “Wait here until I return, I want to chase that beautiful creature,” and he rode into the forest after it, followed only by his animals.The attendants halted and waited until evening, but he did not return, so they rode home, and told the young Queen that the young King had followed a white hart into the enchanted forest, and had not come back again.Then she was in the greatest concern about him.He, however, had still continued to ride on and on after the beautiful wild animal, and had never been able to overtake it; when he thought he was near enough to aim, he instantly saw it bound away into the far distance, and at length it vanished altogether.And now he perceived that he had penetrated deep into the forest, and blew his horn but he received no answer, for his attendants could not hear it.And as night, too, was falling, he saw that he could not get home that day, so he dismounted from his horse, lighted himself a fire near a tree, and resolved to spend the night by it.While he was sitting by the fire, and his animals also were lying down beside him, it seemed to him that he heard a human voice.He looked round, but could perceived nothing.Soon afterwards, he again heard a groan as if from above, and then he looked up, and saw an old woman sitting in the tree, who wailed unceasingly, “Oh, oh, oh, how cold I am!”Said he, “Come down, and warm thyself if thou art cold.”But she said, “No, thy animals will bite me.”He answered, “They will do thee no harm, old mother, do come down.”She, however, was a witch, and said, “I will throw down a wand from the tree, and if thou strikest them on the back with it, they will do me no harm.”Then she threw him a small wand, and he struck them with it, and instantly they lay still and were turned into stone.And when the witch was safe from the animals, she leapt down and touched him also with a wand, and changed him to stone.Thereupon she laughed, and dragged him and the animals into a vault, where many more such stones already lay.
年轻的国王始终没有回来，王后越发地担心了。这个时候，当年分别时选择往东边走的哥哥也来到了这个国家。他没有找到合适的事情做，便四处流浪，让小动物们表演舞蹈。突然一个念头闪过，他决定回去看看当年插在树上的那把刀，那样他就能知道弟弟过得怎么样了。到了之后，他发现向着弟弟的那面锈迹斑斑，但尚有光泽。他有些担心，心想：“弟弟一定遇上困难了，既然刀面尚有光泽，也许我能救出他。”他带着动物们朝西走去，进了城门之后，门卫走上前来，询问是否要禀报公主，并说公主这些天来因为担心他而悲痛欲绝，害怕他在魔法森林里被杀害了。哨兵以为他就是年轻的国王，因为兄弟俩长得太像了，而且后面也跟着蹦蹦跳跳的小动物们。他明白了原来他们说的是他的弟弟，心想：“我不如将错就错，这样就能更顺利地救出他了。”然后他准许门卫将他送回城堡，大家看到他回来都非常高兴。年轻的王后以为这就是自己的丈夫，问他为什么离开那么久。他答道：“我在森林里迷路了，找了好久才找到回来的路。”晚上他被带到皇宫卧室，但却在他和年轻的公主之间放了一把双刃剑。公主很困惑，但又不敢开口问。 As, however, the young King did not come back at all, the Queen’s anguish and care grew constantly greater.And it so happened that at this very time the other brother who had turned to the east when they separated, came into the kingdom.He had sought a situation, and had found none, and had then travelled about here and there, and had made his animals dance.Then it came into his mind that he would just go and look at the knife that they had thrust in the trunk of a tree at their parting, that he might learn how his brother was.When he got there his brother’s side of the knife was half rusted, and half bright.Then he was alarmed and thought, “A great misfortune must have befallen my brother, but perhaps I can still save him, for half the knife is still bright.”He and his animals travelled towards the west, and when he entered the gate of the town, the guard came to meet him, and asked if he was to announce him to his consort the young Queen, who had for a couple of days been in the greatest sorrow about his staying away, and was afraid he had been killed in the enchanted forest.The sentries, indeed, thought no otherwise than that he was the young King himself, for he looked so like him, and had wild animals running behind him.Then he saw that they were speaking of his brother, and thought, “It will be better if I pass myself off for him, and then I can rescue him more easily.”So he allowed himself to be escorted into the castle by the guard, and was received with the greatest joy.The young Queen indeed thought that he was her husband, and asked him why he had stayed away so long.He answered, “I had lost myself in a forest, and could not find my way out again any sooner.”At night he was taken to the royal bed, but he laid a two-edged sword between him and the young Queen; she did not know what that could mean, but did not venture to ask.
他又在王宫里住了几天，同时尽力打听有关魔法森林的消息，最后他说：“我必须要再去那里打猎。”国王和年轻的王后劝他不要去，但是他决心已定，后来带着更多的人马出发了。到了森林里之后，他跟哥哥一样看到了一只白色的雄鹿，然后对随从说：“在这里等我回来，我想去追赶这只可爱的雄鹿。”然后他骑着马冲进森林，他的小动物们在后面跟着。但他却追不上这只雄鹿，在森林里越跑越远，最后不得不在这里过夜了。他升起一堆火，突然听到上面有人哭着喊：“啊，啊，我好冷啊！”然后他抬头看，还是同一个女巫坐在树上。他说：“老太太，如果你冷，就下来暖和一下吧。”她答道：“不，小动物们会咬我的。”但是他说：“他们不会伤害你的。”然后她哭道：“我扔给你一根树枝，你用它抽打它们的背部，它们就不会伤害我了。”猎人听到后，就起了疑心，说道：“我不会打我的动物的。下来吧，否则我把你拽下来。”然后她又哭着说：“你想干嘛啊？你不要碰我。”但是他回答道：”如果你不下来，我就开枪打死你。“她说：“尽管打吧，我不怕你的子弹！”然后他瞄准，向她开火了。但是铅弹头穿不透女巫，她奸笑着说道：“你伤不到我的。”猎人知道要怎么做。他从衣服上撕下三个银制纽扣，装进枪里，因为这能对付女巫的三枚纽扣。他一开枪，女巫惨叫一声，摔在了地上。然后他一脚踩住她，说道：“老巫婆，如果你不说出我的弟弟在哪里，我就把你扔进火里。她吓怕了，求饶说，他和他的动物们现在躺在大坑里，已经成了石头。然后他押着巫婆跟他一起去，并威胁她说：“老东西，如果你不让我弟弟和其他躺在那里的人重新活过来，我就把你扔进火里！”她拿起一根枝条，点了那些石头，然后他的弟弟和小动物们活了过来。其他人，有商人、艺术家、牧羊人，都纷纷站起来感谢他的救命之恩，然后便回家了。双胞胎兄弟终于相见，激动地抱在一起。然后他们抓住了巫婆，把她绑起来放到火上，巫婆被烧死了之后，森林自动地向两边分开了，远处就是国王的王宫，走路估计需要三个小时。 He remained in the palace a couple of days, and in the meantime inquired into everything which related to the enchanted forest, and at last he said, “I must hunt there once more.”The King and the young Queen wanted to persuade him not to do it, but he stood out against them, and went forth with a larger following.When he had got into the forest, it fared with him as with his brother; he saw a white hart and said to his people, “Stay here, and wait until I return, I want to chase the lovely wild beast,” and then he rode into the forest and his animals ran after him.But he could not overtake the hart, and got so deep into the forest that he was forced to pass the night there.And when he had lighted a fire, he heard some one wailing above him, “Oh, oh, oh, how cold I am!”Then he looked up, and the self-same witch was sitting in the tree.Said he, “If thou art cold, come down, little old mother, and warm thyself.”She answered, “No, thy animals will bite me.”But he said, “They will not hurt thee.”Then she cried, “I will throw down a wand to thee, and if thou smitest them with it they will do me no harm.”When the huntsman heard that, he had no confidence in the old woman, and said, “I will not strike my animals.Come down, or I will fetch thee.”Then she cried, “What dost thou want?Thou shalt not touch me.”But he replied, “If thou dost not come, I will shoot thee.”Said she, “Shoot away, I do not fear thy bullets!”Then he aimed, and fired at her, but the witch was proof against all leaden bullets, and laughed, and yelled and cried, “Thou shalt not hit me.”The huntsman knew what to do, tore three silver buttons off his coat, and loaded his gun with them, for against them her arts were useless, and when he fired she fell down at once with a scream.Then he set his foot on her and said, Old witch, if thou dost not instantly confess where my brother is, I will seize thee with both my hands and throw thee into the fire.She was in a great fright, begged for mercy and said. He and his animals lie in a vault, turned to stone.Then he compelled her to go thither with him, threatened her, and said, Old sea-cat, now shalt thou make my brother and all the human beings lying here, alive again, or thou shalt go into the fire!She took a wand and touched the stones, and then his brother with his animals came to life again, and many others, merchants, artizans, and shepherds, arose, thanked him for their deliverance, and went to their homes.But when the twin brothers saw each other again, they kissed each other and rejoiced with all their hearts.Then they seized the witch, bound her and laid her on the fire, and when she was burnt the forest opened of its own accord, and was light and clear, and the King’s palace could be seen at about the distance of a three hours walk.
于是兄弟俩一起回家了，路上相互讲着各自的故事。弟弟说道自己是这片国土的统治者时，哥哥说：“我已经发现了，因为当我冒充你进城时，受到了王室隆重地接待，年轻的王后以为我是她的丈夫，我不得不同她一起吃饭，并在她的床上睡觉。”弟弟听到后，非常嫉妒气愤，拔出宝剑，砍掉了哥哥的脑袋。当他意识到哥哥死了，看到鲜血直流，他万分后悔，悲恸地喊道：“我的哥哥救了我啊，我却恩将仇报。”说完大哭起来。然后他的兔子跑上来，主动要求去摘些回生草。它蹦蹦跳跳地去了，并及时带着仙草回来了。哥哥重新活过来了，完全不晓得发生了什么。 Thereupon the two brothers went home together, and on the way told each other their histories.And when the youngest said that he was ruler of the whole country in the King’s stead, the other observed, “That I remarked very well, for when I came to the town, and was taken for thee, all royal honours were paid me; the young Queen looked on me as her husband, and I had to eat at her side, and sleep in thy bed.”When the other heard that, he became so jealous and angry that he drew his sword, and struck off his brother’s head.But when he saw him lying there dead, and saw his red blood flowing, he repented most violently: “My brother delivered me,” cried he, “and I have killed him for it,” and he bewailed him aloud.Then his hare came and offered to go and bring some of the root of life, and bounded away and brought it while yet there was time, and the dead man was brought to life again, and knew nothing about the wound.
他们继续往前走着。弟弟说：“我们长相相似，穿着同样的王服，后面跟着同样的动物。我们从相反的门进去吧，从两边同时到达年迈的国王面前。”因此他们分开走了。门卫分别从两边的门同时进来禀报说年轻的国王和他的小动物们狩猎回来了。国王说道：“不可能，两扇门隔着一英里远呢。”然而，兄弟俩同时从相反的方向走进王宫大院，一起踏上台阶。然后国王对公主说：“谁是你的丈夫啊？他们太像了，我分不出来。”公主十分沮丧，她无法分辨。但最后公主想起了她送给小动物们的项链。一番搜寻后，她在狮子身上发现了金扣子，她激动地哭了：“这只狮子跟着的那位就是我真正的丈夫。”然后年轻的国王笑了，说道：“是的，完全正确。”他们在餐桌前坐下来，欢快地享用着盛宴。晚上，年轻的国王上床后，妻子说：“前几天晚上为什么你总在我们的床上放一把双刃剑呢？我还以为你想杀我呢。”然后他明白了哥哥对自己是多么地忠心。 After this they journeyed onwards, and the youngest said, “Thou lookest like me, hast royal apparel on as I have, and the animals follow thee as they do me; we will go in by opposite gates, and arrive at the same time from the two sides in the aged King’s presence.”So they separated, and at the same time came the watchmen from the one door and from the other, and announced that the young King and the animals had returned from the chase.The King said, “It is not possible, the gates lie quite a mile apart.”In the meantime, however, the two brothers entered the courtyard of the palace from opposite sides, and both mounted the steps.Then the King said to the daughter, “Say which is thy husband.Each of them looks exactly like the other, I cannot tell.”Then she was in great distress, and could not tell; but at last she remembered the necklace which she had given to the animals, and she sought for and found her little golden clasp on the lion, and she cried in her delight, “He who is followed by this lion is my true husband”.Then the young King laughed and said, “Yes, he is the right one,” and they sat down together to table, and ate and drank, and were merry.At night when the young King went to bed, his wife said, “Why hast thou for these last nights always laid a two-edged sword in our bed?I thought thou hadst a wish to kill me.”Then he knew how true his brother had been.
两个旅行者 The Two Travellers
山丘和山谷从不会碰到一起，而人类的后代，无论是善是恶，却总会相遇。就这样，一个鞋匠和一个裁缝在他们的旅途中相逢了。裁缝是个英俊的小伙子，他总是很快乐、十分乐观。看见鞋匠从另一边向自己走来时，从他背的包裁缝就猜出了他的职业，于是便唱了一小段歌来嘲弄鞋匠： Hill and vale do not come together, but the children of men do, good and bad.In this way a shoemaker and a tailor once met with each other in their travels.The tailor was a handsome little fellow who was always merry and full of enjoyment.He saw the shoemaker coming towards him from the other side, and as he observed by his bag what kind of a trade he plied, he sang a little mocking song to him,
“为我缝一缝裂开的缝，帮我拉拉紧松开的线，把沥青涂在鞋子边上，用钉子把鞋头敲敲紧。” “Sew me the seam, Draw me the thread, Spread it over with pitch, Knock the nail on the head.”
然而，鞋匠却无法忍受这个玩笑。他拉长了脸，如同刚喝了醋一般，做了个手势像要去掐裁缝的脖子。但小裁缝却笑了起来，递过他的瓶子说道：“我并没有恶意，喝一口吧，把你的怒气压下去。”鞋匠喝了很大一口，脸上的不悦终于慢慢退去了。他把瓶子还给了裁缝，说：“我要客气地对你说话，一个人总在畅饮之后说好话，口干舌燥时可说不出好话。我们能一起旅行吗？”“没问题。”裁缝回答道，“但愿到大城镇去能合你的心意，那儿有很多的活可干。”“那正是我想去的地方。”鞋匠回道，“在小镇上没什么钱可挣，而在乡下，人们喜欢光脚走路。”于是他们便一同上路了，就像黄鼠狼在雪地里一样，他们总是踩着猫步前进。 The shoemaker, however, could not endure a joke; he pulled a face as if he had drunk vinegar, and made a gesture as if he were about to seize the tailor by the throat.But the little fellow began to laugh, reached him his bottle, and said, “No harm was meant, take a drink, and swallow your anger down.”The shoemaker took a very hearty drink, and the storm on his face began to clear away.He gave the bottle back to the tailor, and said, “I spoke civilly to you; one speaks well after much drinking, but not after much thirst.Shall we travel together?”“All right,” answered the tailor, “if only it suits you to go into a big town where there is no lack of work.”“That is just where I want to go,” answered the shoemaker.“In a small nest there is nothing to earn, and in the country, people like to go barefoot.”They travelled therefore onwards together, and always set one foot before the other like a weasel in the snow.
他们并不急着赶路，但是吃的却很少，也没有好好地休息。每当他们抵达一个城镇，他们总会前去拜访商人们，因为裁缝看上去生气勃勃又充满着欢乐，还有着相当红润的脸颊，每个人都很乐意给他活干，运气好的时候，雇主的女儿还会在门廊下给他一个吻。再一次与鞋匠相聚时，总是裁缝包袱里的东西最多。坏脾气的鞋匠一脸挖苦的表情，心里想：“人越无赖，运气就越好。”但是裁缝却又笑又唱，把他得到的一切与同伴分享。如果口袋里有两个便士碰撞得叮当响，他就会好好喝上一杯，愉快地击着桌子，击得许多杯子都跳动起来，对他来说，钱来得容易，去得也很容易。 Both of them had time enough, but little to bite and to break.When they reached a town they went about and paid their respects to the tradesmen, and because the tailor looked so lively and merry, and had such pretty red cheeks, every one gave him work willingly, and when luck was good the master’s daughters gave him a kiss beneath the porch, as well.When he again fell in with the shoemaker, the tailor had always the most in his bundle.The ill-tempered shoemaker made a wry face, and thought, “The greater the rascal the more the luck,” but the tailor began to laugh and to sing, and shared all he got with his comrade.If a couple of pence jingled in his pockets, he ordered good cheer, and thumped the table in his joy till the glasses danced, and it was lightly come, lightly go, with him.
经过一段时间的旅程，他们来到了一片大森林，这是通往首都的必经之路。摆在他们面前的有两条路，一条要走七天，另一条只要两天就能到达，但是两个旅行者都不知道哪一条才是捷径。他们在一棵橡树下坐了下来，商议着接下来要怎么办，要给自己准备多少天的面包。鞋匠说：“一个人一定要三思而后行，我要带上够吃一个星期的面包。”“什么！”裁缝说道，“在背上背七天的粮食就像驼物的牲口一样，还怎么看路。我要相信上帝，不会为任何事烦扰！我口袋里的钱不论夏天还是冬天都一样好用，但是在炎热的天气里，面包会变得干巴巴，再者它还会发霉，甚至我的衣服也无法穿那么久。再说了，为什么我们就找不到那条近的路呢？带上够吃两天的面包就足够了。”就这样，两人分别买了自己所需的面包，到森林里去碰运气去了。 When they had travelled for some time, they came to a great forest through which passed the road to the capital.Two foot-paths, however, led through it, one of which was a seven days’ journey, and the other only two, but neither of the travellers knew which way was the short one.They seated themselves beneath an oak-tree, and took counsel together how they should forecast, and for how many days they should provide themselves with bread.The shoemaker said, “One must look before one leaps, I will take with me bread for a week.”“What!” said the tailor, “drag bread for seven days on one’s back like a beast of burden, and not be able to look about.I shall trust in God, and not trouble myself about anything!The money I have in my pocket is as good in summer as in winter, but in hot weather bread gets dry, and mouldy into the bargain; even my coat does not go as far as it might.Besides, why should we not find the right way?Bread for two days, and that’s enough.”Each, therefore, bought his own bread, and then they tried their luck in the forest.
森林里就像教堂那样寂静无声。没有风的吹拂，没有小溪的潺潺流水，没有鸟儿的歌唱，茂盛的枝叶挡住了阳光的照射。鞋匠一言不发，沉重的面包压得他直不起身，汗水从他那愤怒而又沮丧的脸上流了下来。而裁缝很是欢快，蹦蹦跳跳，用叶子吹着口哨，或是唱唱歌，他暗自想到：“上帝在天堂里看到我如此快乐一定也很高兴。” It was as quiet there as in a church.No wind stirred, no brook murmured, no bird sang, and through the thickly-leaved branches no sunbeam forced its way.The shoemaker spoke never a word, the heavy bread weighed down his back until the perspiration streamed down his cross and gloomy face.The tailor, however, was quite merry, he jumped about, whistled on a leaf, or sang a song, and thought to himself, “God in heaven must be pleased to see me so happy.”
就这样持续了两天，当第三天来临时，他们还没走到森林的尽头，这时裁缝已经把他所有的面包吃完了，他不禁有些失落。与此同时，他没有失去勇气，依然相信上帝和他自己的运气。第三天晚上，饥饿的裁缝躺在一棵树下，第二天早上醒来时，饥饿依然陪伴着他。就这样，第四天也过去了，当鞋匠坐在一棵倒落的树上狼吞虎咽地吃着晚餐时，裁缝只能在一旁眼巴巴看着。如果他乞求想要一小片面包时，鞋匠就会嘲笑挖苦道：“你不是一直很快乐么，现在你能尝一次悲伤的滋味了：早上唱歌太早的鸟儿到了晚上就会被鹰攻击。”总而言之，鞋匠是个毫无同情心的人。到了第五个早晨，可怜的裁缝再也站不起来了，虚弱的他几乎都说不出话来；他面颊苍白、眼睛发红。这时，鞋匠对他说：“今天我可以给你一点面包，但是作为交换，我要把你的右眼挖出来。”不幸的裁缝还是想保住性命，没有办法只能答应鞋匠，他的双眼再一次流下了眼泪，随后便任由鞋匠处置，铁石心肠的鞋匠便用一把锋利的刀把他的右眼挖了出来。裁缝想起了从前他在食品储藏室里偷吃东西时，母亲对她说的话：“吃能吃到的东西，受该遭受的苦。”吃完了那昂贵的面包后，他再次站起来，将痛苦抛在脑后，安慰自己，想着用一只眼他也能看得见。然而到了第六天，饥饿再次袭来，啮咬着他，几乎要咬到心脏。晚上，他倒在一棵树旁，到了第七天的早上，晕眩让他爬都爬不起来，他就快死了。这时，鞋匠说：“我将大发慈悲再给你一些面包，但是不能白给，我要挖出你另外一只眼睛来交换。”现在裁缝终于体会到他对待生命是那样轻率，便向上帝乞求原谅，并说道：“你想怎么做就怎么做吧，我会忍受我该忍受的，但是请记住，上帝不会总是坐视不理的，总有一天，你对我做的这些我不应得的恶行，一定会得到报应的。我风光的时候，我和你分享我的一切。我的职业要求每一针都要和其他针一样精准。如果我失去了双眼，就再也不能做针线活，只能到处去乞讨了。当我瞎了的时候，请你无论如何不要抛下我一个人，否则的话我会饿死的。”而鞋匠，已经将上帝逐出了他的内心，拿起刀挖出了裁缝的左眼。接着，鞋匠给了裁缝一点面包，用棍子牵引着他，让他跟在身后。 This lasted two days, but on the third the forest would not come to an end, and the tailor had eaten up all his bread, so after all his heart sank down a yard deeper.In the meantime he did not lose courage, but relied on God and on his luck.On the third day he lay down in the evening hungry under a tree, and rose again next morning hungry still; so also passed the fourth day, and when the shoemaker seated himself on a fallen tree and devoured his dinner, the tailor was only a looker-on.If he begged for a little piece of bread the other laughed mockingly, and said, “Thou hast always been so merry, now thou canst try for once what it is to be sad: the birds which sing too early in the morning are struck by the hawk in the evening,” In short he was pitiless.But on the fifth morning the poor tailor could no longer stand up, and was hardly able to utter one word for weakness; his cheeks were white, and his eyes red.Then the shoemaker said to him, “I will give thee a bit of bread to-day, but in return for it, I will put out thy right eye.”The unhappy tailor who still wished to save his life, could not do it in any other way; he wept once more with both eyes, and then held them out, and the shoemaker, who had a heart of stone, put out his right eye with a sharp knife.The tailor called to remembrance what his mother had formerly said to him when he had been eating secretly in the pantry.“Eat what one can, and suffer what one must.”When he had consumed his dearly-bought bread, he got on his legs again, forgot his misery and comforted himself with the thought that he could always see enough with one eye.But on the sixth day, hunger made itself felt again, and gnawed him almost to the heart.In the evening he fell down by a tree, and on the seventh morning he could not raise himself up for faintness, and death was close at hand.Then said the shoemaker, “I will show mercy and give thee bread once more, but thou shalt not have it for nothing, I shall put out thy other eye for it.”And now the tailor felt how thoughtless his life had been, prayed to God for forgiveness, and said, “Do what thou wilt, I will bear what I must, but remember that our Lord God does not always look on passively, and that an hour will come when the evil deed which thou hast done to me, and which I have not deserved of thee, will be requited.When times were good with me, I shared what I had with thee.My trade is of that kind that each stitch must always be exactly like the other.If I no longer have my eyes and can sew no more I must go a-begging.At any rate do not leave me here alone when I am blind, or I shall die of hunger.”The shoemaker, however, who had driven God out of his heart, took the knife and put out his left eye.Then he gave him a bit of bread to eat, held out a stick to him, and drew him on behind him.
太阳下山时，他们走出了森林，而在他们面前开阔的乡间上竖着绞刑架。鞋匠把失明的裁缝指引到那里，丢下他一个人独自上路了。疲劳、痛苦夹杂着饥饿让这个可怜的人睡着了，一睡就是一整夜。第二天黎明时分他醒来了，却不知道自己身在何处。在绞刑架上吊着两个可怜的罪人，每个人的头上都坐着一只乌鸦。其中一个被吊着的人开口说道：“兄弟，你醒了吗？”“是的，我醒了。”第二个回答道。“那我要告诉你一些事情，”第一个人说，“昨晚从绞刑架上滴到我们身上的露水，谁要是用它来清洗就能再次获得他的眼睛。如果盲人知道了，有多少人能够重新恢复视力呢，尽管他们并不相信那有可能。” When the sun went down, they got out of the forest, and before them in the open country stood the gallows.Thither the shoemaker guided the blind tailor, and then left him alone and went his way.Weariness, pain, and hunger made the wretched man fall asleep, and he slept the whole night.When day dawned he awoke, but knew not where he lay.Two poor sinners were hanging on the gallows, and a crow sat on the head of each of them.Then one of the men who had been hanged began to speak, and said, “Brother, art thou awake?”“Yes, I am awake,” answered the second.“Then I will tell thee something,” said the first; “the dew which this night has fallen down over us from the gallows, gives every one who washes himself with it his eyes again.If blind people did but know this, how many would regain their sight who do not believe that to be possible.”
裁缝听到了这番话，他掏出了口袋里的手帕，把它按在草地上，等手帕被露水湿润后便用它来清洗眼窝。顷刻间，绞刑架上那个人的话便实现了，一对健康的新眼睛从眼窝里长了出来。很快，裁缝便看到了太阳从群山后升起，他面前的平原上矗立着一座伟大的皇城，有着壮丽的大门和数以百计的高塔，金色的球和十字架在高塔的塔尖闪闪发光。他能清楚地辨别树上的每一片叶子，看见每一只飞过的鸟，还有空气中飞舞的每一只飞虫。他从口袋里掏出一根针，又能和从前一样灵巧地穿针引线了，这让他的心里荡漾着愉悦。他跪倒在地，感谢上帝对他的仁慈，并且做了晨祷。他没有忘记为那两个可怜的罪人也做了祷告，那两个人吊在那里，被风吹得互相碰撞，就好像钟摆那样左摇右摆。随后，他把包袱扛在背上，很快就忘却了内心曾受过的痛苦，唱着小曲、吹着口哨上路了。 When the tailor heard that, he took his pocket-handkerchief, pressed it on the grass, and when it was moist with dew, washed the sockets of his eyes with it.Immediately was fulfilled what the man on the gallows had said, and a couple of healthy new eyes filled the sockets.It was not long before the tailor saw the sun rise behind the mountains; in the plain before him lay the great royal city with its magnificent gates and hundred towers, and the golden balls and crosses which were on the spires began to shine.He could distinguish every leaf on the trees, saw the birds which flew past, and the midges which danced in the air.He took a needle out of his pocket, and as he could thread it as well as ever he had done, his heart danced with delight.He threw himself on his knees, thanked God for the mercy he had shown him, and said his morning prayer.He did not forget also to pray for the poor sinners who were hanging there swinging against each other in the wind like the pendulums of clocks.Then he took his bundle on his back and soon forgot the pain of heart he had endured, and went on his way singing and whistling.
他所遇见的第一样东西是一匹在田间自由奔跑的棕色小马驹。他抓住了它的鬃毛，想要跳到它身上骑着进城。然而小马驹却乞求裁缝放了它。“我依然还很幼小。”它说，“即使是像你这样重量轻的裁缝也会把我的背压成两半，让我走吧，直到我变得强壮起来。到那个时候我会报答你的。”“走吧，”裁缝说，“我看你还是个小家伙呢。”他用鞭子在小马驹的背上轻抽了一下，于是小马驹欢快地撒开后蹄，越过树篱和沟渠，飞奔向广阔的田野间。 The first thing he met was a brown foal running about the fields at large.He caught it by the mane, and wanted to spring on it and ride into the town.The foal, however, begged to be set free.“I am still too young,” it said, “even a light tailor such as thou art would break my back in two let me go till I have grown strong.A time may perhaps come when I may reward thee for it.”“Run off,” said the tailor, “I see thou art still a giddy thing.”He gave it a touch with a switch over its back, whereupon it kicked up its hind legs for joy, leapt over hedges and ditches, and galloped away into the open country.
但是从前一天起，小裁缝还什么都没有吃。“我的眼里满是阳光，”他说，“但是嘴里却没吃到一口粮食。接下来碰到的第一样东西，只要凑合着能吃，我就一定要用它来充饥。”这时，一只鹳姿态庄重地从草地上向他走来。“停下，停下！”裁缝边喊着边抓住了它的腿。“我不知道你吃起来是否美味，但是我饥肠辘辘，没有其他好的选择。我必须砍下你的头，把你烤着吃。”“不要那样做，”鹳回应说，“我是一只圣鸟，会给人类带来益处的，谁都不应当伤害我。放我一条生路吧，我会用其他方式来让你受益的。”“好吧，你走吧，长腿兄弟。”裁缝说道。鹳立起身，把它长长的腿悬在下面，优雅地飞走了。 But the little tailor had eaten nothing since the day before.“The sun to be sure fills my eyes,” said he, “but the bread does not fill my mouth.The first thing that comes across me and is even half edible will have to suffer for it.”In the meantime a stork stepped solemnly over the meadow towards him.“Halt, halt!” cried the tailor, and seized him by the leg.“I don’t know if thou art good to eat or not, but my hunger leaves me no great choice.I must cut thy head off, and roast thee.”“Don’t do that,” replied the stork; “I am a sacred bird which brings mankind great profit, and no one does me an injury.Leave me my life, and I may do thee good in some other way.”“Well, be off, Cousin Longlegs,” said the tailor.The stork rose up, let its long legs hang down, and flew gently away.
“这样何时才是尽头啊？”终于，裁缝自言自语道，“我越来越饿了，我的胃里越来越空了。我在路上碰到那么多，现在都丢失了。就在这时，他看见池塘里有两只小鸭子游向他。“你们来的正是时候。”他说着便伸手抓住其中一只，准备拧断它的脖子。在这节骨眼上，一只躲藏在芦苇丛中的老鸭子大声尖叫起来，张着喙向他游来，急切地恳求他放过自己亲爱的孩子。“你能想象得出，”老鸭子说，“假如有人想要把你抓走，并且杀了你，你的母亲会有多么哀伤？”“别说了，”好脾气的裁缝说道，“带你的孩子走吧。”于是便把刚才抓住的小鸭子放回了水里。 “What’s to be the end of this?” said the tailor to himself at last, “my hunger grows greater and greater, and my stomach more and more empty.Whatsoever comes in my way now is lost.”At this moment he saw a couple of young ducks which were on a pond come swimming towards him.“You come just at the right moment,” said he, and laid hold of one of them and was about to wring its neck.On this an old duck which was hidden among the reeds, began to scream loudly, and swam to him with open beak, and begged him urgently to spare her dear children.“Canst thou not imagine,” said she, “how thy mother would mourn if any one wanted to carry thee off, and give thee thy finishing stroke?”“Only be quiet,” said the good-tempered tailor, “thou shalt keep thy children,” and put the prisoner back into the water.
当他转过身来时，他正站在一棵老树前，树的一部分已经空了，他看见一些野蜂在飞进飞出。“我的善行立刻就得到回报了。”裁缝说，“蜂蜜可以恢复我的精力。”蜂后却飞了出来，扬言说：“如果你伤害我的子民，破坏我的巢穴，我们的刺会像一万根烧红的针一样蛰在你的皮肤上。但是如果你不打扰我们，走你自己的路，我们以后会找机会帮助你的。” When he turned round, he was standing in front of an old tree which was partly hollow, and saw some wild bees flying in and out of it.“There I shall at once find the reward of my good deed,” said the tailor, “the honey will refresh me.”But the Queen-bee came out, threatened him and said, “If thou touchest my people, and destroyest my nest, our stings shall pierce thy skin like ten thousand red-hot needles.But if thou wilt leave us in peace and go thy way, we will do thee a service for it another time.”
小裁缝一看这里也没什么可吃的。“前三个盘子都落空了，第四个也什么都没有，真是顿糟糕的晚餐！”于是他拖着饥肠辘辘的身子向城里走去，当时十二点的钟声刚好敲响，小旅馆中的饭菜都为他做好了，所以他能坐下来，立刻就开饭。酒足饭饱后，他说：“现在，我要开始干活了。”他在城里溜了一圈，寻觅着雇主，很快就找到了一份好差事。然而，他的手艺太精湛了，不久就出名了，每个人都想要一件小裁缝做的新衣裳，他的名声与日俱增。“我的手艺已经到此为止了。”他说，“但我还要每天都有所改进。”最后，国王钦点他成为皇室的裁缝。 The little tailor saw that here also nothing was to be done.“Three dishes empty and nothing on the fourth is a bad dinner!”He dragged himself therefore with his starved-out stomach into the town, and as it was just striking twelve, all was ready-cooked for him in the inn, and he was able to sit down at once to dinner.When he was satisfied he said, “Now I will get to work.”He went round the town, sought a master, and soon found a good situation.As, however, he had thoroughly learnt his trade, it was not long before he became famous, and every one wanted to have his new coat made by the little tailor, whose importance increased daily.“I can go no further in skill,” said he, “and yet things improve every day.”At last the King appointed him court-tailor.
但天下就是有那么巧的事情！就在同一天，小裁缝从前的旅伴，那个鞋匠也成了皇室的鞋匠。当鞋匠看见裁缝，发现裁缝又有了一双完好的眼睛，良心便开始不安起来。他心想：“在他向我报复之前，我一定要给他挖个陷阱。”然而，给他人设陷阱的人，往往会自食其果。到了晚上，当工作都结束、天开始暗下来时，鞋匠偷偷跑到国王那儿说：“国王陛下，裁缝那个傲慢的家伙竟然吹嘘自己可以找回在古时候丢失的那个黄金王冠。”“这我倒是很高兴啊。”国王说，于是第二天一早便召见裁缝，命令他把王冠取回来，否则就永远离开这里。裁缝心想：“噢！无赖总是能编出许多瞎话。如果暴躁的国王要我去做别人都办不到的事，我就不能等到明天早上了，现在，我就要立刻离开。于是，他收拾好自己的包袱，但当他站在大门外的时候，他不禁为放弃了自己的大好际遇、抛弃让他一帆风顺的城镇而难过。他来到了遇到那些鸭子的池塘边，在那里他曾开恩放了一只老鸭子的孩子。此时，这只老鸭子正坐在岸边，用喙梳理着羽毛。她马上认出了他，便询问他为什么耷拉着脑袋？“你要是听到了我的遭遇，你就不会惊讶了。”小裁缝说着便告诉了她自己的命运。“如果就是这些，”鸭子说，“我们可以帮助你。王冠掉到了水里，正在水底躺着呢，我们这就帮你拿上来。同时，你就把你的手帕铺在岸边吧。”她和她的十二个孩子潜到水里，五分钟后她再次浮出水面，王冠就在它的翅膀上，十二只小鸭子在附近游来游去，把他们的喙放在王冠下，帮着一起运上来。他们游到了岸边，把王冠放在了手帕上。谁也想象不到王冠是多么地华丽，当阳光照在上面时，它就像成千上万的红宝石一般闪烁着光芒。裁缝将手帕用四个角系好，拿给了国王。国王高兴坏了，便把一串金项链戴到裁缝的脖子上。 But how things do happen in the world!On the very same day his former comrade the shoemaker also became court-shoemaker.When the latter caught sight of the tailor, and saw that he had once more two healthy eyes, his conscience troubled him.“Before he takes revenge on me,” thought he to himself, “I must dig a pit for him.”He, however, who digs a pit for another, falls into it himself.In the evening when work was over and it had grown dusk, he stole to the King and said, “Lord King, the tailor is an arrogant fellow and has boasted that he will get the gold crown back again which was lost in ancient times.”“That would please me very much,” said the King, and he caused the tailor to be brought before him next morning, and ordered him to get the crown back again, or to leave the town for ever.“Oho!” thought the tailor, “a rogue gives more than he has got.If the surly King wants me to do what can be done by no one, I will not wait till morning, but will go out of the town at once, to-day.”He packed up his bundle, therefore, but when he was without the gate he could not help being sorry to give up his good fortune, and turn his back on the town in which all had gone so well with him.He came to the pond where he had made the acquaintance of the ducks; at that very moment the old one whose young ones he had spared, was sitting there by the shore, pluming herself with her beak.She knew him again instantly, and asked why he was hanging his head so?“Thou wilt not be surprised when thou hearest what has befallen me,” replied the tailor, and told her his fate.“If that be all,” said the duck, “we can help thee.The crown fell into the water, and lies down below at the bottom; we will soon bring it up again for thee.In the meantime just spread out thy handkerchief on the bank.”She dived down with her twelve young ones, and in five minutes she was up again and sat with the crown resting on her wings, and the twelve young ones were swimming round about and had put their beaks under it, and were helping to carry it.They swam to the shore and put the crown on the handkerchief.No one can imagine how magnificent the crown was; when the sun shone on it, it gleamed like a hundred thousand carbuncles.The tailor tied his handkerchief together by the four corners, and carried it to the King, who was full of joy, and put a gold chain round the tailor’s neck.
鞋匠看到一计不成，便再施一计。他跑去对国王说：“国王陛下，裁缝又开始傲慢无礼了，他夸口说能用蜡重塑一个王宫，不论是活动的还是不活动的，里里外外，一样都不会少。”国王便召见裁缝，下令要他用蜡重塑整座王宫，不论活动的还是不活动的，里里外外，一样都不能少，如果他做不到，或是墙上少一根钉子，他都将终身被关在地下。 When the shoemaker saw that one stroke had failed, he contrived a second, and went to the King and said, “Lord King, the tailor has become insolent again; he boasts that he will copy in wax the whole of the royal palace, with everything that pertains to it, loose or fast, inside and out.”The King sent for the tailor and ordered him to copy in wax the whole of the royal palace, with everything that pertained to it, movable or immovable, within and without, and if he did not succeed in doing this, or if so much as one nail on the wall were wanting, he should be imprisoned for his whole life under ground.
裁缝心想：“事情越来越糟了！谁还能忍受那些？”他背起包袱又上路了。他又来到了那棵有空洞的大树前，耷拉着脑袋坐在树下。蜜蜂从树里飞了出来，蜂后看他斜着脑袋，便问他是不是脖子僵硬了。“哎呀，不是这样。”裁缝回答说，“是另有事情让我忧心忡忡。”接着便把国王派给他的任务告诉了蜂后。蜜蜂们开始嗡嗡嗡地互相说话，蜂后说：“回去吧，明天的这个时候带上一张大床单回来，到时候一切都会好起来的。”于是裁缝又折了回去，但蜜蜂们却飞向了王宫，直直地从开着的窗户飞进去，悄悄地爬满每一个角落，格外仔细地观察着一切。随后他们又急急忙忙飞了回去，用蜡建造起了王宫的模型，他们的速度是如此之快，倘若有人在一边看着，一定会以为是在他眼皮底下长起来的。到了晚上，一切都准备就绪了。第二天，当裁缝来的时候，一座壮丽的建筑已经摆在那儿了，墙上的钉子、屋顶上的瓦片，一样都没有少，它还很精致，像白雪一样纯白，还散发着蜂蜜的香甜。裁缝小心翼翼地用布将它包裹起来，呈现给国王，国王对它简直爱不释手，把它摆放在最大的厅里，作为奖赏，赐给了裁缝一座大石头房子。 The tailor thought, “It gets worse and worse!No one can endure that?” and threw his bundle on his back, and went forth.When he came to the hollow tree, he sat down and hung his head.The bees came flying out, and the Queen-bee asked him if he had a stiff neck, since he held his head so awry?“Alas, no,” answered the tailor, “something quite different weighs me down,” and he told her what the King had demanded of him.The bees began to buzz and hum amongst themselves, and the Queen-bee said, “Just go home again, but come back to-morrow at this time, and bring a large sheet with you, and then all will be well.”So he turned back again, but the bees flew to the royal palace and straight into it through the open windows, crept round about into every corner, and inspected everything most carefully.Then they hurried back and modelled the palace in wax with such rapidity that any one looking on would have thought it was growing before his eyes.By the evening all was ready, and when the tailor came next morning, the whole of the splendid building was there, and not one nail in the wall or tile of the roof was wanting, and it was delicate withal, and white as snow, and smelt sweet as honey.The tailor wrapped it carefully in his cloth and took it to the King, who could not admire it enough, placed it in his largest hall, and in return for it presented the tailor with a large stone house.
然而鞋匠却仍然不肯放弃，他第三次对国王说：“国王陛下，裁缝听说城堡的天井里没有喷泉，他扬言他能在天井中间造一口喷泉，水能喷出一个人那么高，像水晶一样清澈。”国王派人把裁缝叫到了跟前，说：“如果到了明天，天井里还没有像你承诺的那样建起一口喷泉，刽子手就要在那里砍了你的脑袋。”可怜的裁缝没有多想便匆匆向城门跑去，这一回对他来说真是生死攸关，眼泪从他的脸上滚落下来。他满怀悲伤地向前走着，那只他曾经放生的小马驹跳到了他的面前，小马驹已经长成了一匹漂亮的栗色大马。“就是现在，”它对裁缝说，“我要报答你的善行。我已经知道你需要什么了，但你很快就会得到帮助，到我的背上来吧，我现在可以驮得住两个你了。”裁缝又重新恢复了勇气，他一下跳上了马背，马便全速向城里飞奔而去，直接进了城堡的天井里。它如闪电一般飞驰了三圈，跑到第三圈时，突然重重地倒在地上。与此同时雷声轰鸣，十分可怕。天井中间的那部分土地像炮弹一样弹到了空中，落在城堡的外面，随即，喷射出一口喷泉，像人骑在马背上那么高，水如同水晶般纯净，阳光照耀着泉水闪闪发光。国王看到眼前这一切，惊讶地站了起来，当着所有人的面，拥抱了裁缝。 The shoemaker, however, did not give up, but went for the third time to the King and said, “Lord King, it has come to the tailor’s ears that no water will spring up in the court-yard of the castle, and he has boasted that it shall rise up in the midst of the court-yard to a man’s height and be clear as crystal.”Then the King ordered the tailor to be brought before him and said, “If a stream of water does not rise in my court-yard by to-morrow as thou hast promised, the executioner shall in that very place make thee shorter by the head.”The poor tailor did not take long to think about it, but hurried out to the gate, and because this time it was a matter of life and death to him, tears rolled down his face.Whilst he was thus going forth full of sorrow, the foal to which he had formerly given its liberty, and which had now become a beautiful chestnut horse, came leaping towards him.“The time has come,” it said to the tailor, “when I can repay thee for thy good deed.I know already what is needful to thee, but thou shalt soon have help; get on me, my back can carry two such as thou.”The tailor’s courage came back to him; he jumped up in one bound, and the horse went full speed into the town, and right up to the court-yard of the castle.It galloped as quick as lightning thrice round it, and at the third time it fell violently down.At the same instant, however, there was a terrific clap of thunder, a fragment of earth in the middle of the court-yard sprang like a cannon-ball into the air, and over the castle, and directly after it a jet of water rose as high as a man on horseback, and the water was as pure as crystal, and the sunbeams began to dance on it.When the King saw that he arose in amazement, and went and embraced the tailor in the sight of all men.
但是好景不长。国王有许多女儿，一个比一个漂亮，但是却没有儿子。于是，恶毒的鞋匠第四次向国王进言道：“国王陛下，裁缝依然不改他的傲慢自大。这一次他吹嘘说，只要他愿意，他可以从空气中给国王带来一个儿子。”国王命令传召裁缝，对他说：“如果你在九天内为我带来一个儿子，我就把大女儿嫁给你。”小裁缝心想：“这个奖赏确实很不错，我愿意为了它而做些什么。但是对我来说樱桃长得太高了，如果我要爬上去摘它们，脚下的树枝会断裂，我就会摔下去的。” But good fortune did not last long.The King had daughters in plenty, one still prettier than the other, but he had no son.So the malicious shoemaker betook himself for the fourth time to the King, and said, “Lord King, the tailor has not given up his arrogance.He has now boasted that if he liked, he could cause a son to be brought to the Lord king through the air.”The King commanded the tailor to be summoned, and said, “If thou causest a son to be brought to me within nine days, thou shalt have my eldest daughter to wife.”“The reward is indeed great,” thought the little tailor; “one would willingly do something for it, but the cherries grow too high for me, if I climb for them, the bough will break beneath me, and I shall fall.”
他回到家，盘腿坐在逢衣桌前，思索着要如何是好。最后他大喝一声：“根本不可能办得到，我要远走高飞，归根结底，我无法在这里平静地生活了。”他收拾起包袱，急忙向大门跑去。当他来到草地时，他认出了他的老朋友鹳，鹳正像个哲学家一样前后踱步。有时候，他站在那里一动不动，对一只青蛙端详良久，最后还是把青蛙吞下肚。鹳走上前来与小裁缝打招呼。鹳开口说：“我看见了你背上背着包袱。你为什么要离开这里呢？”裁缝便把国王要求他做的事情告诉了鹳，他是不可能完成的，说着便为自己的不幸感到悲痛。“不要为了这事愁白了头。”鹳说道，“我会帮助你走出困境的。我为城里送去包裹在襁褓中的婴儿已经很长时间了，所以这一次，说不定我能从井里接来一位小王子。回家去吧，别担心了。从这一刻开始的第九天，你就到皇宫去，我也会到那儿去的。”小裁缝回到了家，到了约定的那一天，便来到了王宫。不一会儿，鹳就飞了过来，轻轻叩击着窗户。裁缝为它打开窗，长腿兄弟便小心翼翼地走了进来，迈着庄重的步伐走在大理石铺成的光滑路面上。另外，它的喙叼着一个小婴孩，他可爱得就像一个天使，还把他的小手伸向了王后。鹳把婴儿放在了王后的大腿上，王后爱抚着并亲吻着婴儿，高兴得不能自已。鹳离开之前，从背上拿下了旅行包，把它递给了王后。在包里有一些纸做的小包，里面是分给小公主们五颜六色的蜜饯。但是大公主没有分到，她得到了快乐的小裁缝做丈夫。“对我来说，”小裁缝说，“这就好像是我赢得了最高的奖赏。我母亲总是对的，她常常说凡是信仰上帝的人总是会有好运气的，不会失败。” He went home, seated himself cross-legged on his work-table, and thought over what was to be done.“It can’t be managed,” cried he at last, “I will go away; after all I can’t live in peace here.”He tied up his bundle and hurried away to the gate.When he got to the meadow, he perceived his old friend the stork, who was walking backwards and forwards like a philosopher.Sometimes he stood still, took a frog into close consideration, and at length swallowed it down.The stork came to him and greeted him.“I see,” he began, “that thou hast thy pack on thy back.Why art thou leaving the town?”The tailor told him what the King had required of him, and how he could not perform it, and lamented his misfortune.“Don’t let thy hair grow grey about that,” said the stork, “I will help thee out of thy difficulty.For a long time now, I have carried the children in swaddling-clothes into the town, so for once in a way I can fetch a little prince out of the well.Go home and be easy.In nine days from this time repair to the royal palace, and there will I come.”The little tailor went home, and at the appointed time was at the castle.It was not long before the stork came flying thither and tapped at the window.The tailor opened it, and cousin Longlegs came carefully in, and walked with solemn steps over the smooth marble pavement.He had, moreover, a baby in his beak that was as lovely as an angel, and stretched out its little hands to the Queen.The stork laid it in her lap, and she caressed it and kissed it, and was beside herself with delight.Before the stork flew away, he took his travelling bag off his back and handed it over to the Queen.In it there were little paper parcels with colored sweetmeats, and they were divided amongst the little princesses.The eldest, however, had none of them, but got the merry tailor for a husband.“It seems to me,” said he, “just as if I had won the highest prize.My mother was if right after all, she always said that whoever trusts in God and only has good luck, can never fail.”
而鞋匠只能为小裁缝做婚礼庆典穿的舞鞋，从那以后他便被永远逐出了城。那条通往森林的路把他带到了绞刑架前。心中的怒火加上炎热的天气让鞋匠精疲力尽，他倒了下来。他闭上眼睛准备睡上一觉，两只乌鸦却从被吊在那儿的绞刑犯头上飞了下来，啄出了他的眼睛。鞋匠疯狂地向森林里跑去，最后一定饿死在那里了，因为从此之后再也没有人见过他，或是听到过他的消息。 The shoemaker had to make the shoes in which the little tailor danced at the wedding festival, after which he was commanded to quit the town for ever.The road to the forest led him to the gallows.Worn out with anger, rage, and the heat of the day, he threw himself down.When he had closed his eyes and was about to sleep, the two crows flew down from the heads of the men who were hanging there, and pecked his eyes out.In his madness he ran into the forest and must have died there of hunger, for no one has ever either seen him again or heard of him.
忘恩负义的儿子 The Ungrateful Son
从前，有一个男人和他的妻子坐在家门边，他们正准备一起吃摆放在面前的一只烤鸡。这时，那个男人看到他年迈的父亲正朝他们走来，他匆忙拿起鸡，把它藏了起来，因为他不许父亲吃一丁点烤鸡。老人来了后，喝了口酒便离开了。现在儿子想要把烤鸡重新端上桌子，但是一拿起来，鸡却变成了一只巨大的癞蛤蟆。癞蛤蟆跳到这个男人的脸上，便不再离去，如果谁想把它拿走，它便恶狠狠地看着那人，仿佛要跳到那人的脸上去，因此没有人敢碰它。这个忘恩负义的儿子被迫每天给癞蛤蟆喂食，不然的话癞蛤蟆就会咬他的脸来填饱肚子。从此这个男人只能四处漂泊，不得安宁。 A man and his wife were once sitting by the door of their house, and they had a roasted chicken set before them, and were about to eat it together.Then the man saw that his aged father was coming, and hastily took the chicken and hid it, for he would not permit him to have any of it.The old man came, took a drink, and went away.Now the son wanted to put the roasted chicken on the table again, but when he took it up, it had become a great toad, which jumped into his face and sat there and never went away again, and if any one wanted to take it off, it looked venomously at him as if it would jump in his face, so that no one would venture to touch it.And the ungrateful son was forced to feed the toad every day, or else it fed itself on his face; and thus he went about the world without knowing rest.
白蛇 The White Snake
很久很久以前，有一位国王。由于拥有过人的智慧而闻名全国。他无所不晓，仿佛最机密的事情都会通过空气传到他耳中。但是，他有一个奇怪的习惯，就是在用完每天的晚餐，饭桌收拾完毕，众人均退下后，一位最受信赖的仆人，会为他端上另一个盘子。然而，这个盘子有盖子盖着，没有人知道里面盛了些什么，就连这个仆人也不知道。因为国王要等到只有一个人时，才会打开盖子享用这道菜。 A long time ago there lived a king who was famed for his wisdom through all the land.Nothing was hidden from him, and it seemed as if news of the most secret things was brought to him through the air.But he had a strange custom; every day after dinner, when the table was cleared, and no one else was present, a trusty servant had to bring him one more dish.It was covered, however, and even the servant did not know what was in it, neither did anyone know, for the King never took off the cover to eat of it until he was quite alone.
就这样过了很久。有一天这个仆人送菜时，由于实在按捺不住心中的好奇，不禁将其端回了自己房间。他仔细地锁好门，掀开盖子，发现在盘子里放着的是一块白蛇肉。当他看到白蛇肉后，便无法打消尝尝鲜的念头，因而他割下一小块肉，送进嘴里。他的舌头刚碰到白蛇肉，便听到从窗外传来了一阵奇怪的声音，好似窃窃私语一般。于是，他走了过去，仔细听后才发现原来那是一群正在聊天的麻雀，它们正在互相交流着在树林里和原野上的见闻。由于偷吃了白蛇肉，他现在可以听懂动物们说话了。 This had gone on for a long time, when one day the servant, who took away the dish, was overcome with such curiosity that he could not help carrying the dish into his room.When he had carefully locked the door, he lifted up the cover, and saw a white snake lying on the dish.But when he saw it he could not deny himself the pleasure of tasting it, so he cut off a little bit and put it into his mouth.No sooner had it touched his tongue than he heard a strange whispering of little voices outside his window.He went and listened, and then noticed that it was the sparrows who were chattering together, and telling one another of all kinds of things which they had seen in the fields and woods.Eating the snake had given him power of understanding the language of animals.
恰好在这一天，王后弄丢了她最漂亮的一枚戒指。这位国王最信任的仆人成了众矢之的，大家都怀疑他，因为只有他可以在宫中随意走动。国王命令把这个仆人带到自己面前，火冒三丈地威胁他说，如果到第二天还不能供出小偷，那么就认为他有罪，并将他处死。这个仆人宣称自己是清白的，但也无济于事。国王没有给他一个更好的答复，只叫他退下。 Now it so happened that on this very day the Queen lost her most beautiful ring, and suspicion of having stolen it fell upon this trusty servant, who was allowed to go everywhere.The King ordered the man to be brought before him, and threatened with angry words that unless he could before the morrow point out the thief, he himself should be looked upon as guilty and executed.In vain he declared his innocence; he was dismissed with no better answer.
他又着急又害怕，跑到庭院里，想着如何使自己摆脱这个困境。这时，有几只鸭子安静地坐在一条小河边休息。它们一边用自己的喙把羽毛梳理平整，一边聊着私密的话题。于是这个仆人便站在它们旁边，仔细听着它们的对话。它们正在互相谈论着早上逛过的所有地方，在那些地方又都找了些什么好吃的。其中有一只鸭子，难受地说：“我肚子里有个沉甸甸的东西。我早上吃得太快，把王后窗下的戒指吞进了肚子里。”这个仆人立即一把抓住它的脖子，拎着它来到御膳房，对厨师说：“这只鸭子够肥了，请把它宰了吧。”“好嘞，”厨师接过鸭子，掂了掂分量，接着说，“它为了喂肥自己没少花功夫啊，就等着被烤了。”就这样，厨师剁下鸭头，正当他把鸭子的内脏取出来，准备用烤叉串好时，就在鸭子的肚子里发现了王后的戒指。 In his trouble and fear he went down into the courtyard and took thought how to help himself out of his trouble.Now some ducks were sitting together quietly by a brook and taking their rest; and, whilst they were making their feathers smooth with their bills, they were having a confidential conversation together.The servant stood by and listened.They were telling one another of all the places where they had been waddling about all the morning, and what good food they had found, and one said in a pitiful tone, “Something lies heavy on my stomach; as I was eating in haste I swallowed a ring which lay under the Queen’s window.”The servant at once seized her by the neck, carried her to the kitchen, and said to the cook, “Here is a fine duck; pray, kill her.”“Yes,” said the cook, and weighed her in his hand; “she has spared no trouble to fatten herself, and has been waiting to be roasted long enough.”So he cut off her head, and as she was being dressed for the spit, the Queen’s ring was found inside her.
这样一来，仆人很容易地证明了自己的清白。而国王为了弥补自己的过失，答应这个仆人可以帮他一个忙，并且承诺，他可以挑选他想要的皇宫中的最好职位。这个仆人全部谢绝，只是要求国王赏赐了一匹马和一些钱作为旅费，因为他很想去看看外面的世界，四处走一走。 The servant could now easily prove his innocence; and the King, to make amends for the wrong, allowed him to ask a favor, and promised him the best place in the court that he could wish for.The servant refused everything, and only asked for a horse and some money for traveling, as he had a mind to see the world and go about a little.
仆人的要求得到了满足，便上路了。有一天，他来到一个池塘附近，看到三条鱼为芦苇叶所困，因缺水而透不过气来。尽管人们都说鱼儿不会说话，但是他听到鱼儿们叹息说，它们一定会非常凄惨地死去。这个仆人有一颗善良的心，他从马背上下来，把三条被困的鱼儿送回了水中。三条鱼高兴得颤抖不已，从水中探出头来，对他喊道：“我们一定会记住你的，我们一定会报答你的救命之恩！” When his request was granted he set out on his way, and one day came to a pond, where he saw three fishes caught in the reeds and gasping for water.Now, though it is said that fishes are dumb, he heard them lamenting that they must perish so miserably, and, as he had a kind heart, he got off his horse and put the three prisoners back into the water.They quivered with delight, put out their heads, and cried to him, “We will remember you and repay you for saving us!”
于是他骑上马继续前行。过了一会儿，他好像听到从他脚下的沙子里传来了声音。他仔细聆听，发现原来是一只蚁王的抱怨：“为什么人类和他们的那些笨重的野兽不能不压在我们身上呢？那匹蠢马的蹄子那么重，一直如此残忍地践踏我的子民！”于是，他改走了旁边的一条小路。蚁王对他喊道：“我们会记住你的——好人有好报！” He rode on, and after a while it seemed to him that he heard a voice in the sand at his feet.He listened, and heard an ant-king complain, “Why cannot folks, with their clumsy beasts, keep off our bodies?That stupid horse, with his heavy hoofs, has been treading down my people without mercy!”So he turned on to a side path and the ant-king cried out to him, ‘We will remember you—one good turn deserves another!”
沿着小路他进入了一片森林，在森林里，他看到有两只老乌鸦站在它们的巢穴边，正在往外赶小乌鸦。它们喊道：“滚开！你们这帮好吃懒做的家伙！我们不能再为你们找食物了，你们已经长大了，能自力更生了！”然而这些可怜的小乌鸦们一个个摔在了地上，拍打着翅膀，喊道：“啊，我们太小，太无助了！我们必须自己找食物生活，但是我们还不会飞！除了躺在这里挨饿，我们还能做什么？”于是，这个好心的年轻人跳下来，拔剑斩马，作为小乌鸦们的食物。于是，小乌鸦们争先恐后地蹦过来争抢食物，填饱了肚子。它们喊道：“我们会记住你的——好人有好报！” The path led him into a wood, and here he saw two old ravens standing by their nest, and throwing out their young ones.“Out with you, you idle, good-for-nothing creatures!” cried they; “we cannot find food for you any longer; you are big enough, and can provide for yourselves.”But the poor young ravens lay upon the ground, flapping their wings, and crying, “Oh, what helpless chicks we are!We must shift for ourselves, and yet we cannot fly!What can we do, but lie here and starve?”So the good young fellow alighted and killed his horse with his sword, and gave it to them for food.Then they came hopping up to it, satisfied their hunger, and cried, “We will remember you—one good turn deserves another!”
现在，这个年轻人只能步行了。他走了很远很远的路，来到了一座大城市。大街上人头攒动，熙熙攘攘。这时，一个骑马的人大声喊道：“公主正在招驸马，谁想娶她，就必须完成一个艰巨的任务，如果任务失败了，他就会丧命。”很多人都已经做过尝试，但都失败了。然而，当这个年轻人看到公主时，就被其天仙般的容貌所征服。他忘记了所有的风险，来到国王面前，声称自己是驸马的合适人选。 And now he had to use his own legs, and when he had walked a long way, he came to a large city.There was a great noise and crowd in the streets, and a man rode up on horseback, crying aloud, “The King’s daughter wants a husband; but whoever sues for her hand must perform a hard task, and if he does not succeed he will forfeit his life.”Many had already made the attempt, but in vain; nevertheless when the youth saw the King’s daughter he was so overcome by her great beauty that he forgot all danger, went before the King, and declared himself a suitor.
于是他被带到了海边。当着他的面，一枚金戒指被扔进了海里。随后，国王命令他把戒指从海底捞上来，并且说道：“如果你上来时没有捞到戒指，就会被一次又一次地扔进大海，直到海浪把你吞没为止。”所有人都为这位英俊的年轻人伤心。然后他们纷纷离去，留他独自一人在海边。 So he was led out to the sea, and a gold ring was thrown into it, in his sight; then the King ordered him to fetch this ring up from the bottom of the sea, and added, “If you come up again without it you will be thrown in again and again until you perish amid the waves.”All the people grieved for the handsome youth; then they went away, leaving him alone by the sea.
他站在岸边，正琢磨着该怎么办时，突然看到三条鱼向他游来。这三条鱼，正是他以前搭救过的三条鱼。当中的那条嘴里衔着一只珠蚌，它将珠蚌放在岸上这个年轻人的脚下。年轻人捡起珠蚌，打开一看，发现那枚金戒指就躺在珠蚌的壳里。他喜出望外，把戒指交给国王，满心期盼着国王能兑现自己的诺言，将女儿许配给他作为回报。 He stood on the shore and considered what he should do, when suddenly he saw three fishes come swimming towards him, and they were the very fishes whose lives he had saved.The one in the middle held a mussel in its mouth, which it laid on the shore at the youth’s feet, and when he had taken it up and opened it, there lay the gold ring in the shell.Full of joy he took it to the King, and expected that he would grant him the promised reward.
但是当高傲的公主得知这个年轻人的出身配不上自己时，便十分轻视他，提出他必须再完成一个任务。公主下楼来到院子里，亲手将整整十袋的小米撒在草坪上，而后说道：“明天太阳升起前，你必须捡起地上所有的小米，一粒也不能少。” But when the proud princess perceived that he was not her equal in birth, she scorned him, and required him first to perform another task.She went down into the garden and strewed with her own hands ten sacks-full of millet-seed on the grass; then she said, “To-morrow morning before sunrise these must be picked up, and not a single grain be wanting.”
这个年轻人坐在院子里，思考着该如何完成这个任务，但是他毫无办法，他悲伤地坐在那里，等着天亮，等着被处以死刑。但是，当太阳的第一缕阳光照进院子时，他发现十只袋子并排放在那里，每个袋子都是满满的，一粒小米都没有少。原来是蚁王，在半夜带着成千上万的蚂蚁们赶来。这些对年轻人心存感激的蚂蚁，不辞劳苦地将地上的小米一一捡起，收集起来放进袋子里。 The youth sat down in the garden and considered how it might be possible to perform this task, but he could think of nothing, and there he sat sorrowfully awaiting the break of day, when he should be led to death.But as soon as the first rays of the sun shone into the garden he saw all the ten sacks standing side by side, quite full, and not a single grain was missing.The ant-king had come in the night with thousands and thousands of ants, and the grateful creatures had by great industry picked up all the millet-seed and gathered them into the sacks.
不久，公主亲自来到院子里，看到年轻人已经完成了自己交给他的任务，大为吃惊。然而，她还是敌不过自己高傲的心，说道：“尽管他已经完成了两个任务，但是，除非他为我摘到生命树上的苹果，否则他别想成为我的丈夫。” Presently the King’s daughter herself came down into the garden, and was amazed to see that the young man had done the task she had given him.But she could not yet conquer her proud heart, and said, “Although he has performed both the tasks, he shall not be my husband until he has brought me an apple from the Tree of Life.”
年轻人不知道生命树在哪里，但他还是出发了。虽然他对找到生命树没抱什么希望，但是，只要他的两条腿走得动，他就会永远找下去。一天晚上，他来到一片树林，这时，他已经走遍了三个王国了。他在一棵树下躺下，准备休息。这时，他听到树枝间传来沙沙的声音，然后一只金苹果便掉落在他的手里。这时，三只乌鸦飞下来，落在他的膝盖上，并且说道：“我们就是那三只你曾经搭救过的小乌鸦，因为你，我们才没有被饿死。我们长大后，听说你正在寻找金苹果，我们便飞越重洋，来到长着生命树的世界尽头，把金苹果摘下给你带回来了。”年轻人大喜过望，踏上归程，把金苹果呈给国王漂亮的女儿，她再也找不到借口了。他们将生命树上的苹果一切为二，一起分享了这个苹果。然后，她的心中充满了对他的爱。最终，他们白头偕老，一生平安快乐。 The youth did not know where the Tree of Life stood, but he set out, and would have gone on for ever, as long as his legs would carry him, though he had no hope of finding it.After he had wandered through three kingdoms, he came one evening to a wood, and lay down under a tree to sleep.But he heard a rustling in the branches, and a golden apple fell into his hand.At the same time three ravens flew down to him, perched themselves upon his knee, and said, “We are the three young ravens whom you saved from starving; when we had grown big, and heard that you were seeking the Golden Apple, we flew over the sea to the end of the world, where the Tree of Life stands, and have brought you the apple.”The youth, full of joy, set out homewards, and took the Golden Apple to the King’s beautiful daughter, who had no more excuses left to make.They cut the Apple of Life in two and ate it together; and then her heart became full of love for him, and they lived in undisturbed happiness to a great age.
技艺超群的乐师 The Wonderful Musician
从前，有一个技艺超群的乐师。他独自一人走在森林里，思考着各种各样的事。等到没什么可想的时候，他自言自语道：“一个人在森林里的日子开始难熬了，我得给自己找个好伙伴。”于是，他从背上取下小提琴拉了起来；琴声荡漾在整个森林里。拉了不一会儿，一只狼穿过灌木丛一路小跑过来。“啊，来了一只狼！我可不想跟它一起！”乐师说，但是狼已经走近了，对他说：“啊，亲爱的乐师，你演奏的曲子好美。我也想学呢。”“这很好学的，”乐师答道，“你只要按我说的去做就行了。”“哦，乐师，”狼说，“我会像学生听老师的话那样服从您的。”乐师让狼跟着他走。他们一起走了一段路，来到了一棵大树前。这是一棵中空的老橡树，树干中间裂了一个大缝。“看，”乐师说，“如果你想学拉小提琴的话，就把你的前爪放在这个裂缝里。”狼照做了，但乐师迅速捡起一块石头砸过去，将狼的这两只爪子紧紧卡在了裂缝里，于是狼不得不像一个囚犯一样呆在那儿了。“在我回来之前呆在那儿别动。”乐师说完就离开了。 There was once a wonderful musician, who went alone through a forest and thought of all manner of things, and when nothing was left for him to think about, he said to himself, “Time is beginning to pass heavily with me here in the forest, I will fetch hither a good companion for myself.”Then he took his fiddle from his back, and played so that it echoed through the trees.It was not long before a wolf came trotting through the thicket towards him.“Ah, here is a wolf coming!I have no desire for him!” said the musician; but the wolf came nearer and said to him, “Ah, dear musician, how beautifully thou dost play.I should like to learn that, too.”“It is soon learnt,” the musician replied, “thou hast only to do all that I bid thee.”“Oh, musician,” said the wolf, “I will obey thee as a scholar obeys his master.”The musician bade him follow, and when they had gone part of the way together, they came to an old oak-tree which was hollow inside, and cleft in the middle.“Look,” said the musician, “if thou wilt learn to fiddle, put thy fore paws into this crevice.”The wolf obeyed, but the musician quickly picked up a stone and with one blow wedged his two paws so fast that he was forced to stay there like a prisoner.“Stay there until I come back again,” said the musician, and went his way.
过了一会儿，乐师又自言自语道：“一个人在森林里的日子开始难熬了，我得给自己找个好伙伴。”于是他又拿出小提琴，在森林里拉了起来。没过多久，一只狐狸穿过树丛偷偷地朝他走过来了。“啊，来了一只狐狸！”乐师说道，“我可不想跟它一起。”狐狸走上前去对乐师说：“哦，亲爱的乐师，您弹奏的曲子好美啊！我也想学呢。”“这很好学的，”乐师说道，“你只要照我说的做就行了。”“啊，乐师，”狐狸说，“我会像学生听老师的话那样服从您的。”“跟我来。”乐师说；他们走了一段路以后，来到了一条两边有高高的灌木丛的小路上。这时，乐师站住不走了。他先把小路一边的一棵小榛树弯到地面，再用脚踩住，又把小路另一边的一棵小树也弯到地上，然后他说：“喂，小狐狸，如果你想学什么东西的话，把你的左前爪给我。”狐狸照他说的做了，然后乐师就把他的爪子绑在了左边的树枝上。“小狐狸，”他说，“现在把你的右前爪给我。”他又把它绑在了右边的树枝上。在检查完绑得足够结实之后，乐师松开了脚，于是这两棵树便再次弹起来，把小狐狸猛地弹了上去，悬在了半空中。“在这儿等我回来。”乐师说完，又继续上路了。 After a while he again said to himself, “Time is beginning to pass heavily with me here in the forest, I will fetch hither another companion.” and took his fiddle and again played in the forest.It was not long before a fox came creeping through the trees towards him.“Ah, there’s a fox coming!” said the musician.“I have no desire for him.”The fox came up to him and said, “Oh, dear musician, how beautifully thou dost play!I should like to learn that too.”“That is soon learnt,” said the musician.“Thou hast only to do everything that I bid thee.”“Oh, musician,” then said the fox, “I will obey thee as a scholar obeys his master.”“Follow me,” said the musician; and when they had walked a part of the way, they came to a footpath, with high bushes on both sides of it.There the musician stood still, and from one side bent a young hazel-bush down to the ground, and put his foot on the top of it, then he bent down a young tree from the other side as well, and said, “Now little fox, if thou wilt learn something, give me thy left front paw.”The fox obeyed, and the musician fastened his paw to the left bough.“Little fox,” said he, “now reach me thy right paw” and he tied it to the right bough.When he had examined whether they were firm enough, he let go, and the bushes sprang up again, and jerked up the little fox, so that it hung struggling in the air.“Wait there till I come back again,” said the musician, and went his way.
乐师又自言自语道：“一个人在森林里的日子开始难熬了，我得给自己找个好伙伴。”因此他又拉起了小提琴，让音乐在森林中回响。这时，一只小野兔向他跳了过来。“哦，来了一只野兔，”乐师说，“我可不想跟它一起。”“啊，亲爱的乐师，”野兔说，“你拉的小提琴曲好美啊，我也想学呢。”“这很好学，”乐师说，“你只要照我说的去做就好了。” Again he said to himself, “Time is beginning to pass heavily with me here in the forest, I will fetch hither another companion,” so he took his fiddle, and the sound echoed through the forest.Then a little hare came springing towards him.“Why, a hare is coming,” said the musician, “I do not want him.”“Ah, dear musician,” said the hare, “how beautifully thou dost fiddle; I too, should like to learn that.”“That is soon learnt,” said the musician, “thou hast only to do everything that I bid thee.”
“哦，乐师，”小野兔答道，“我会像学生听老师的话一样服从您的。”他们一起走了一段路，来到了森林里的一片空地上，那里有一棵山杨树。乐师用一条长绳系住小野兔的脖子，又把绳子的另一端系在了树上。“好了，我活泼的小野兔，绕着树跑二十圈吧！”乐师大声说。小野兔照着做了，但当它绕着树跑完二十圈后，绳子也绕着树缠了二十圈，于是野兔被缠在了树干上，而且无论它怎么拉怎么扯，都只能使绳子在它脆弱的脖子上勒得更深。“在这儿等我回来。”乐师说完，又继续走了。 “Oh, musician,” replied the little hare, “I will obey thee as a scholar obeys his master.”They went a part of the way together until they came to an open space in the forest, where stood an aspen tree.The musician tied a long string round the little hare’s neck, the other end of which he fastened to the tree.“Now briskly, little hare, run twenty times round the tree!” cried the musician, and the little hare obeyed, and when it had run round twenty times, it had twisted the string twenty times round the trunk of the tree, and the little hare was caught, and let it pull and tug as it liked, it only made the string cut into its tender neck.“Wait there till I come back,” said the musician, and went onwards.
在此期间，狼不断地又推又拉地咬那块石头，折腾了好久，最后终于把脚从裂缝里再次抽了出来，可以自由活动了。狼愤怒不已，向乐师离开的方向紧追过去，一心想把他撕成碎片。狐狸看到狼跑过，便开始哀号，并用尽全身的力气喊到：“狼兄弟，快来帮我啊，那个乐师辜负了我！”狼拉下了那棵小树，把绳子咬成两断，救出了狐狸，然后带着狐狸一起去找乐师报仇。它们又看到了被缠在树上的野兔，于是把野兔也救了出来，然后一起去找它们的仇人。 The wolf, in the meantime, had pushed and pulled and bitten at the stone, and had worked so long that he had set his feet at liberty and had drawn them once more out of the cleft.Full of anger and rage he hurried after the musician and wanted to tear him to pieces.When the fox saw him running, he began to lament, and cried with all his might, “Brother wolf, come to my help, the musician has betrayed me!”The wolf drew down the little tree, bit the cord in two, and freed the fox, who went with him to take revenge on the musician.They found the tied-up hare, whom likewise they delivered, and then they all sought the enemy together.
这时，乐师又一次在路上拉起了他的小提琴。这一次，他比较幸运。琴声飘入了一个穷伐木工人的耳朵里。他立刻情不自禁地放下了手中的工作，把斧子挟在腋下走过来听音乐。“我想要的同伴终于来了，”乐师说，“因为我要找一个人作伴，而不是一只野兽。”于是，他开始弹奏了，把乐曲弹奏得那么美丽而欢快，以至于那个穷伐木工人站在原地，像是被施了魔法似的，心中充满了快乐。就在此时，狼、狐狸和野兔出现了，伐木工人一眼就看出它们来者不善。于是，他举起被磨得锃亮的斧头站在乐师的前面，好像在说：“谁要是想碰他就给我小心着点儿，因为要动他就得先跟我斗！”于是，这些野兽都被吓得跑回了森林里。然而，乐师出于谢意，把曲子又给伐木工人演奏了一遍，之后就一个人上路走了。 The musician had once more played his fiddle as he went on his way, and this time he had been more fortunate.The sound reached the ears of a poor wood-cutter, who instantly, whether he would or no, gave up his work and came with his hatchet under his arm to listen to the music.“At last comes the right companion,” said the musician, “for I was seeking a human being, and no wild beast.”And he began and played so beautifully and delightfully that the poor man stood there as if bewitched, and his heart leaped with gladness.And as he thus stood, the wolf, the fox, and the hare came up, and he saw well that they had some evil design.So he raised his glittering axe and placed himself before the musician, as if to say, “Whoso wishes to touch him let him beware, for he will have to do with me!”Then the beasts were terrified and ran back into the forest.The musician, however, played once more to the man out of gratitude, and then went onwards.
年轻的巨人 The Young Giant
从前有个农夫，他有个儿子跟拇指一般大小，而且再没长大过，多年来他连一根头发丝的粗细也没长过。一天，父亲要出门耕地，小东西说：“爸爸，我要和你一起出去。”“你想同我一起出去？”父亲说。“呆在这儿，你在那里没什么用，而且你可能会走丢的！”大拇指听了便哭起来，为了耳根清净他父亲只好将他放入衣兜，带他一起走了。等到出了门来到田间，父亲再把他拿出来放到一个新开的犁沟里。大拇指在犁沟里呆着的时候，一个巨人从山那头过来。“看到那个巨大的妖怪了吗？”父亲说，为了吓唬小东西好让他乖些，“他要来抓你啦。”可是，巨人的长腿没跨两步就来到沟前。他用两根手指小心翼翼地拈起小小的大拇指，仔细打量了他一番，什么也没说就把他带走了。他的父亲站在一边，可吓得吐不出半个字来，他只想着他的孩子丢了，他有生之年再也看不到孩子了。 Once on a time a countryman had a son who was as big as a thumb, and did not become any bigger, and during several years did not grow one hair’s breadth.Once when the father was going out to plough, the little one said, “Father, I will go out with you.”“Thou wouldst go out with me?” said the father.“Stay here, thou wilt be of no use out there, besides thou mightest get lost!”Then Thumbling began to cry, and for the sake of peace his father put him in his pocket, and took him with him.When he was outside in the field, he took him out again, and set him in a freshly-cut furrow.Whilst he was there, a great giant came over the hill.“Do thou see that great bogie?” said the father, for he wanted to frighten the little fellow to make him good; “he is coming to fetch thee.”The giant, however, had scarcely taken two steps with his long legs before he was in the furrow.He took up little Thumbling carefully with two fingers, examined him, and without saying one word went away with him.His father stood by, but could not utter a sound for terror, and he thought nothing else but that his child was lost, and that as long as he lived he should never set eyes on him again.
但是巨人把他带回家，给他喂自己的奶吃，大拇指吃了巨人的奶竟开始长大，而且变得又高又壮，没多久也长成了一个巨人。两年过去后，老巨人带他到森林里，想要试试他，便说：“你自己折一根枝条来看看。”这时，男孩已经非常强壮，便连根从土里拔起一棵小树。但是巨人想：“我们定要比这个厉害才是。”就又带他回去，又喂了他两年的奶。当巨人再试他的时候，大拇指的力气已经大到可以从地里拔起一棵老树。巨人对此仍不满足；他又一次喂了他两年奶，再带他去森林的时候，巨人说道：“现在就给我拔一棵像样的树来。”男孩抱起一棵最粗壮的橡树，不费吹灰之力，大树便应声而起。“这样才行，”巨人说，“你学成啦。”便将他带回田埂，正是以前巨人把他带走的那个地方。他的父亲正在那儿种田。年轻的巨人朝他走去，说：“父亲看呀，您的儿子已长成个多棒的小伙子啦！” The giant, however, carried him home, suckled him, and Thumbling grew and became tall and strong after the manner of giants.When two years had passed, the old giant took him into the forest, wanted to try him, and said, “Pull up a stick for thyself.”Then the boy was already so strong that he tore up a young tree out of the earth by the roots.But the giant thought, “We must do better than that,” took him back again, and suckled him two years longer.When he tried him, his strength had increased so much that he could tear an old tree out of the ground.That was still not enough for the giant; he again suckled him for two years, and when he then went with him into the forest and said, “Now just tear up a proper stick for me,” the boy tore up the strongest oak-tree from the earth, so that it split, and that was a mere trifle to him.“Now that will do,” said the giant, “thou art perfect,” and took him back to the field from whence he had brought him.His father was there following the plough.The young giant went up to him, and said, “Does my father see what a fine man his son has grown into?”
农夫惊惧万分，说：“不，你不是我的儿子；我不要你，离开我！”“我真的是您的儿子；让我帮您干活吧，我犁地能犁得像您一样好，不，比您还好。”“不，不，你不是我儿子；你怎么能犁地呢，快走开！”可是，由于害怕这个巨人，他丢下犁耙，向后退，站到田埂一边去了。年轻人便拿起犁耙，只用一只手压了压，但他那一抓太有力了，犁耙深深嵌进地里。农夫不忍再看这幅景象，向他喊道：“你要是真心想犁地，就不要压得这么重，那样子活儿可干不好。”年轻人呢，索性解下所有马身上的犁，自己拉起来，边犁边说：“您就回去吧，父亲，告诉母亲准备一大盘吃的，一会儿工夫我就能把地犁好了。”农夫只得回家，让妻子准备吃的；年轻人只身一人就犁完了整整两亩的田，犁完地他又挽上耙子，双耙齐下，把整块田都耙完了。干完了活儿，他到树林里拔了两棵橡树，将它们扛上双肩，然后在一边前面挂上耙子，后面也挂上耙子，在另一边前面挂上一匹马，后面也挂上一匹马，就像挑一捆稻草似的挑起这些东西，回他父母亲的家了。他踏进院子时，母亲没有认出他，就问道：“这个可怕的巨人是谁啊？”农夫说：“是我们的儿子。”她说：“不，他不可能是我们的儿子，我们从没有这么高的儿子，我们的儿子是个小不点儿。”她冲着他喊道：“走开，我们不要你！”年轻人沉默不语，只是把马儿拉进马厩，喂它们燕麦、干草，以及其他所需之物。干完这些活，他才进屋，在长椅上坐了下来，说：“母亲，我现在想吃东西，能快点开饭吗？”她说：“好的。”然后端来两个巨大的盛满食物的盘子，这些东西够她和她丈夫吃上一个星期。可是，年轻人一个人就吃光了所有东西，还问她有没有更多东西给他吃。“没有了，”她答道，“我们只有这些。”“但是这只够我尝个鲜儿，我还得吃更多的东西。”母亲哪敢违命，便跑去灶上置了满满一大锅的食物，等吃的东西做好，把锅端了进来。“终于有点东西来填肚子了。”巨人说罢，吃完了所有的东西，但这些还不足以让他吃饱。他又说道：“父亲，我是明白啦，和你们过，我永远都吃不饱；若是你能给我找一样坚硬铁器，硬到放到我膝盖上也顶不断，我倒是可以去外面闯荡。”农夫高兴了，把他两匹马套上车，驱车去铁匠那里取回一样又长又厚的铁器，两匹马才把它拖回来。年轻人把它横放在膝盖上一顶，只听见“啪”的一声！他像摘豆秆一样把铁器从中间一折为二，顺手把它扔了。 The farmer was alarmed, and said, “No, thou art not my son; I don’t want thee leave me!”“Truly I am your son; allow me to do your work, I can plough as well as you, nay better.”“No, no, thou art not my son; and thou canst not plough go away!”However, as he was afraid of this great man, he let go of the plough, stepped back and stood at one side of the piece of land.
